Page 8

Shandong Province's Native Products Oversupply

Cotton, Peanuts, and Wheat Piled Up

Total Value Reaches 10 Million Yuan

Jinan Correspondence: Shandong Province is rich in local products, surpassing Hebei and Henan. Cotton production is mainly concentrated in Linqing, Xiazhen, and Gaotang. This year's total harvest is 800,000 bales. Cotton from Nangong and Wuqiao in southern Hebei is also coming to Jinan for sale. Peanuts are abundant in the Tai'an area of southern Shandong, and goods from Linpu, Qidong, and Lijin also converge in Jinan. Wheat is produced everywhere, with Xuzhou and Yanzhou in the south, and Pingyuan and Yuancheng in the north being the most abundant areas. In addition, there are black dates in western Shandong and tobacco along the Jiaoji Railway in eastern Shandong, which are sold to several provinces in the north and south. This year's black dates had a poor harvest, and although the tobacco harvest was good, the tobacco company refused to buy it, and the value plummeted, only half of what it was in previous years. However, its trading center is not in Jinan. In previous years, when local products were put on the market, the trading was at its peak, and merchants from all over gathered in Jinan to set up shops and buy them, with sales reaching far and wide, thus activating the rural economy and making Jinan exceptionally prosperous. However, after the May 3rd Incident, Jinan became a dead city. In recent years, it has been affected by the global economic recession, local product exports have been cut off, and the market has been depressed. This year's cotton, peanuts, and wheat harvests have been very abundant, but sales are blocked and piled up in Jinan, estimated to be worth about 10 million yuan. Local product merchants are losing money and complaining endlessly, and farmers are also earning little from a year of hard work due to the falling prices of goods. The collapse of the rural economy has created a serious phenomenon. Now that the year is coming to an end, there is probably not much trading to be done. The situation of the accumulation of various local products is described as follows:

(Cotton) Since the new cotton came on the market in September this year, it has been transported to Jinan. Although the Shanghai merchants have been buying, they have not been very keen due to the arrival of American cotton. After the Japanese merchants boycotted Indian cotton, they purchased Shandong cotton, but they did not import much. State-owned yarn factories, such as Qingdao Huaxin, Jinan Lufeng, and Chengtong, etc., are not very enthusiastic about purchasing due to poor yarn sales. The price, which was previously 44 or 45 yuan, is now 38 or 39 yuan, and every day 1,000 to 2,000 bales of spot goods are traded and futures are shipped out, while at the same time 1,000 to 2,000 bales are also imported every day. After offsetting the two figures, the total cotton stock in the city is now 125,000 bales, with an average price of 60 yuan per bale, worth about 7.5 million yuan.

(Peanuts) The peanut sales channel has become very narrow. Qingdao merchants and Japanese merchants are not buying in large quantities, and only Guangdong merchants are purchasing, but the amount is also small. When it first came on the market, it was 5.45 yuan, but now it is only 4.12 yuan. Since the Fujian issue, the Guangdong merchants have also purchased rarely. In the past half month, local merchants have purchased and stored peanuts because the price of peanuts has fallen to the lowest limit, and there have been slight transactions every day, but they are not actual sales. Only a few hundred tons are traded every day. The total storage of peanuts in the city is more than 130,000 bales, with each bale calculated at more than 7 yuan, worth about 1 million yuan.

(Wheat) The Jinan Grain Industry Association is the general mechanism for grain transactions. At its peak, there were more than 100 companies involved in transactions, but now there are only more than 30. Transactions are mainly wheat. This year, the flour mills are not operating well and are losing money, so they are shrinking their scope to maintain support. The output has decreased and the purchase of wheat is also rare. In the past week, due to the New Year's relationship, the factories have not purchased. Good wheat in Jiehe and other places is now only more than 3.30 yuan. The total storage in the city is 160,000 bales, worth about 1.3 million yuan.

As for Shandong's cattle hides, they have always been a major export product. The Cattle Hide Bureau's income was more than 910,000 yuan in the 19th year of the Republic, 900,000 yuan in the 20th year, and 580,000 yuan in the 21st year. As of August this year, it has only received 280,000 yuan, and the current income is almost zero. The decline of export goods is so great that it is no wonder the rural areas are so desolate. (December 24th)

Rural Revival Committee Investigates Tea Industry in Huizhou

Fu Hongzhen is dispatched to Huizhou

To discuss ways to save the tea industry

Wuyuan Correspondence: The Rural Revival Committee of the Executive Yuan believes that the decline of Chinese tea has reached its extreme, and methods should be found to save it to recover this dwindling source of profit. It has specially appointed Fu Hongzhen as a specialist investigator of the tea industry in Anhui Province. Mr. Fu arrived in Tunxi a few days ago and visited the leaders of the tea industry in the town to discuss future relief methods and solicit opinions. He also entrusted the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to publicize that the bureau has been ordered by the Ministry of Industry to strictly ban the coloring of Chinese tea, and distributed the bureau's non-toxic improved colorants to various tea shops for application, in order to enhance international credibility and avoid being criticized and excluded by foreigners. Wang Qiupu, chairman of the town's Tea Industry Association, convened a meeting of all tea merchants to welcome him, and fully contributed the crux and weaknesses of the decline of the tea industry, and jointly sought a way out. During the meeting, Fu sharply pointed out the gains and losses of the tea industry, and published the reasons for the plunder of Chinese tea sales as follows: "I have been ordered to investigate and publicize the original intention of banning colored tea, and to persuade the use of alternative non-toxic improved colorants. Southern Anhui is a concentration point for green tea in Anhui, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi. Recently, Chinese tea has been plundered in the overseas market by Indian, Ceylon, Javanese, Japanese, and Taiwanese tea, and the Chinese tea market is on the verge of danger due to the global economic downturn. In the most prosperous year, the output value of tea in Tunxi was 5 or 6 million silver dollars, and the Chouxin Zhenmei tea was as high as more than 300 taels. In the past two years, the Tunxi tea market has been unusually sluggish. Last year, the French government promulgated Article 3 of the regulations for the entry of Chinese tea into French territories, which stipulates that green tea mixed with various teas and colored with indigo, turmeric, talc, or gypsum is prohibited from being sold. Indigo is commonly used by merchants, so there is no problem with blue color. The use of turmeric is slightly astringent, which is actually not without obstruction. The most important thing to prohibit is the yellow aluminum acid and the green arsenic, which contain toxic substances. Tea is originally a beneficial health drink, and its production should be clean, so that it can cater to the needs of consumers. However, Chinese tea is adulterated and faked, and improper colorants such as indigo, foreign blue, turmeric, and lead are added in order to make it look beautiful, or even gypsum, salt, and iron filings are used to increase the weight. Thirty years ago, Australia discovered that Chinese tea was mixed with tree roots, leaves, or old tea mixed with viscous substances, and the inferior appearance was revealed after brewing, reputation was reduced, and capital suffered losses. This kind of immoral behavior damages the credibility of foreign trade, and is enough to give India and Ceylon useful publicity. Decades ago, the world tea market was exclusively occupied by Chinese tea and ranked first in the country's export trade. Now it has been reduced to sixth place, below hides and eggs. The quantity of exports has been reduced by one-half in the past 60 years, while the world's need for tea has increased from 300 million pounds to more than 900 million pounds. In recent decades, Indian, Japanese, and Ceylon tea production has been surplus, and a dumping policy has been implemented, so if we want to revive Chinese tea, we must improve the colorants in order to improve the quality." It is heard that after Mr. Fu completes his investigation in Tunxi, he will go to other counties under Huizhou, as well as Ningguo, Taiping, Guangde, and Xuancheng, and Chun'an and Changhua in Zhejiang Province, for investigation. (December 18th)

Overview of the Current Situation in Guangxi Province

Guangxi Province has achieved remarkable results since being governed by Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi after the 18th year of the Republic. An overview of its situation is as follows:

Vast Land and Sparse Population: Guangxi Province borders French Annam to the southwest and is actually a southern shield for our country. The area is 218,923 square kilometers, mostly mountainous. According to the survey in the 20th year of the Republic, the population is 10,560,500, with an average of 49 people per square kilometer. Compared with Jiangsu Province, which has an area of 105,605 square kilometers and a population of 34,125,857, with an average of 323 people per square kilometer, there is a difference of more than six times. Therefore, the land is vast and the population is sparse. The lack of cultivation of mountain land, allowing it to be barren, is common from Wuzhou to Nanning.

Simple Folk Customs: Guangxi Province has many Yao and Zhuang people. During the Song Dynasty, Nong Zhigao of the Li people occupied Yongning and ruled the entire Guangxi. It was quelled by General Di Qing leading his army. The Kunlun Pass, recorded in history, is located at the intersection of Yongning and Binyang. Most of Di's army was from Shandong, and their descendants have flourished. The people of Guangxi mostly wear cloth clothes and eat coarse grains, and are brave and strong. Women are quite capable and operate no differently than men.

Local Tranquility: The late Qing Dynasty folk saying goes, "In Guangxi Province, there is no land without mountains, no mountains without caves, no caves without bandits." For border officials, transferring to Guangxi was a daunting task. Since the 18th year of the Republic, bandits have been gradually cleared, and the wounds of the Guangdong-Guangxi war have gradually recovered over the years. The province's income is about 30 million yuan per year, which is less than half of Guangdong's, and its distribution is three-fifths for government expenses and two-fifths for military expenses. Education expenses account for 75% of government expenses. The annual government expenditure in Guixian County is 120,000 yuan, and the education expenditure is 90,000 yuan. There are currently about 20 regiments of troops, and local security is mostly maintained by the militia. Soldiers' monthly salaries are 12 yuan, paid on time every month, with no arrears, so military discipline is very good.

Organizing the Militia: The Guangxi Military and Political Conference in the 20th year of the Republic resolved to

Adopt the eight-character policy of "Resisting Japan, Suppressing Communists, Being Friendly, and Being Good Neighbors." In recent years, it has been engaged in political training, cultivating the people's armed forces, implementing autonomy, developing education, and developing the economy at the same time. The results of organizing and training the militia are quite remarkable. The method is to conscript men aged 25 to 40 as regular militia soldiers, train them for six months, and then discharge them. Each time half of the militia soldiers are discharged, the training period is six months, and conscription is held every three months. When the current term is about to expire, the next term will be conscripted to continue training. During the period of enlistment, the monthly salary is paid jointly by the government and local governments, with the proportion being half each. The province is divided into seven districts: Nanning, Guilin, Baise, Tianbao, Wuzhou, Longzhou, and each district has a command headquarters with a commander. Each county has a command headquarters with a commander, who is currently concurrently held by the county magistrate, and a deputy commander is appointed by someone who is familiar with military affairs. Below the county level, there are three types of joint teams, brigades, and squads in districts, townships, and villages, which are under the command of the highest military organ stationed in the province and supervised and guided by the provincial government. Militia soldiers are classified into: (1) Regular Force: selected and trained from the reserve militia soldiers in various counties in the district; (2) Reserve Force: assigned after the training period of the regular militia soldiers; (3) Reserve Force: composed of all conscriptable men in various counties, and when needed, a cadre training team is established, which is composed of retired military officers, sergeants, and graduates of higher primary schools or students with equivalent education selected from various counties in the district. As for the weapons needed by the regular force, in addition to issuing them, the number lacking is temporarily borrowed from the people by the county militia command headquarters. Flags are erected and forts are built in important locations, and one or two militiamen are stationed to protect local travel. The suppression of bandits in Guangxi Province has been successful, and it is indeed due to the effective work of the army in suppressing them, but it also depends entirely on the assistance of the militia.

Engaging in Political Training: Guangxi Province promotes autonomy, militia, education, and economy in one piece. Autonomy is not separated from official duties. Below the province and county levels, there are districts, townships (towns), villages (streets, homes). The district chief, township chief, and village chief also concurrently serve as the joint team leader, brigade leader, and squad leader of the militia. The district, township, and village offices are the militia team headquarters. The future plan is to set up a school in each district, township, and village. The principal also concurrently serves as the village chief and militia team leader. The school is the team headquarters and village office. Farmers' banks and cooperatives in various townships and villages are located in the school, and the head of the school is in charge of economic construction. The most capable and honorable person in the local area is the principal.

Party Headquarters in Secret: The Guangxi Provincial Party Headquarters has temporarily stopped recruiting new party members, and the county party headquarters and below are implementing secret work. Each county only has a communications office, with a secretary to handle external affairs. The names of the members of the Party Central Committee are not publicly announced. The government handles affairs according to the decisions of the Party Headquarters. The chairman and members of the provincial government and the county magistrates also serve as members of the Party Headquarters to avoid separation. There is now no more conflict between the party and the government.

Developed Highways: Guangxi Province's highways are very developed. In addition to the provincial roads that run through the entire province, each county also has county roads, which are all passable by cars. For example, from Wuzhou to Nanning is 1,110 li, and the entire journey is in the mountains and ridges. The road surface is very wide, and the road base is very solid. Although it is winding and continuous, the car travels very smoothly. Vehicles passing through are charged a road maintenance fee of 20%. Also, from Rongxian to Nanning, the one-way fare is 150 yuan. The road maintenance project is supervised by the county government of the location through which it passes, and the villagers provide funds and labor.

Abundant Products: When imported goods enter the country, the Guangxi Provincial Government appropriately increases taxes to protect domestic products and strives for self-sufficiency. As for future economic construction, it has decided to first organize water conservancy, dredge ditches, to facilitate transportation, encourage industry, promote textiles, sugar making, papermaking, planting ramie, and mining, and then study cotton planting and improve the method of making tung oil. According to investigations, the situation of Guangxi's products is as follows: (1) Cultivated Land: In the 6th and 7th years of the Republic, the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce reported that there were more than 80 million mu. The estimate of the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government and reports from various parties show that the total area of paddy fields in the province is about 28 million mu, so there should be more than 50 million mu of reclaimed land and forest land. Rice is the most important crop, with a total output of 45 million dan in the province, with yields ranging from more than 160 jin to more than 340 jin per mu. Next are wheat, corn, sorghum, millet, sweet potatoes, peanuts, soybeans, sugarcane, tea, cotton, ramie, indigo, etc. The output of soybeans and sugarcane is very large. (2) Fishery and Animal Husbandry: Bees, producing cattle, horses, pigs, sheep, chickens, ducks, geese, and pigeons. There are many goats. Horses are purely small species, and their efficiency is far inferior to those produced in Mongolia and Gansu, but they are more agile and also commendable. The annual silk production is 161,695 jin, worth 696,056 yuan. Many counties raise bees, but they do not know how to use new methods. (3) Forestry: Publicly operated are the Liujiang Forest Reclamation Area Office's Liucheng, Liuzhou, Yishan, and Guerong Forest Farms, Fangqiao, Chalu, and Xixiang Forest Farms in the Nanning area, and the Junshan Tung Farm, the Guilin Forest Farm in the Guilin area, the Baise Forest Farm in the Tiannan area, the Longzhou Forest Farm in the Southern area, and the privately operated ones are the most prosperous in the Liujiang area. From the 16th year of the Republic to June of the 21st year, a total of more than 237,000 mu of wasteland was distributed. Timber is the main forest product, with an annual production of 100,000 dan of tung oil, but unfortunately the quality is not pure, and foreign trade is not prosperous. Tea oil is 200,000 dan, cassia oil is 1,000 dan, and anise oil is 2,000 dan, with a total value of 7.35 million. (4) Minerals: Guangxi Province is rich in minerals, with tin and manganese being the most famous. There are provincial-run tin mines in Fuchuan, Hexian, Zhongshan, Nandan, and Hechi, covering an area of 72,360 mu. The remaining minerals such as gold, silver, copper, iron, lead, zinc, bismuth, tungsten, barium, antimony, arsenic, mercury, gypsum, asbestos, saltpeter, and sulfur have a total annual output of 3,404,704 yuan. The sales channels for manganese and antimony have always been Japan. After the September 18th Incident, they have all been suspended. If capital can be invested and new methods are used, fully exploiting them would truly be a great natural source of wealth. However, Guangxi Province is known for being poor and lacking capital. Most commercial operations have small capital and use indigenous mining methods, resulting in very low output, which makes it a pity to abandon the goods on the ground. The coal reserves are estimated to be 300 million tons, and iron is 23.125 million tons. (5) Industry: Guangxi's industry is still immature. Publicly operated factories include the provincial-run sulfuric acid factory, the Guangxi Machinery Factory, the Guangxi Alcohol Factory, the Nanning Leather Factory, the Guangxi Printing Bureau, and six people's factories in Fuchuan, Hezhou, and Zhongshan counties. Privately operated factories are all small capital. Handicrafts such as cotton weaving, porcelain, leather, paper, cigarette cutting, brewing, flour, and firecrackers have a total annual production value of 14,552,808 yuan. (6) Commerce: Statistics from Wuzhou, Nanning, and Longzhou show that imports exceeded exports by 12,230,669 yuan.

Yongding Militia Infighting After the Fujian Incident

Mediation Attempts by Various Parties Fail Repeatedly

Fujian Authorities Have No Time to Attend to Both Military Suppression and Pacification

Shantou Correspondence: In Yongding, Southern Fujian, clashes erupted between Li Yuying's militia and the militia led by Yongding County Magistrate Hu Daonan in the early part of this month in Zhongkeng over the collection of general merchandise taxes (i.e., transit taxes). Hu Daonan was defeated and retreated to the mountain top. Zhongkeng, being Hu's hometown, suffered unexpected losses, with Hu's buildings being burned down. According to Yongding natives in Shantou, the truth of the matter is roughly as follows: Jinfengjiao Pit in Yongding County is a vital land route for cargo transportation between Fujian and Guangdong. The militia has established various tax bureaus there, collecting a large amount of revenue from merchandise taxes. Previously, the Yongding County Public Office sent personnel to collect these taxes. However, after the sudden change in the situation in western Fujian some time ago, Wang Mingchen, the tax collector, absconded with the funds. As a result, Li Yuying, the head of the Zhongkeng Jinfeng District and Hulei Jiaokeng militias, appointed Li Guisan as the tax collector, responsible for collecting all taxes and levies in that area. Ostensibly, it was said that all tax revenue would be distributed fairly to support all the Jinfeng militia, but neither the upper nor lower Jinfeng militia received any benefit. Local people generally did not interfere, as the public taxes were supposed to be managed publicly. When Guangdong Army Commander Huang Renbin took over the defense of Yongding, the Yongding militia, in order to unite internally and cooperate effectively, held a joint meeting in Xiayang on October 22nd. They decided to establish a county-wide defense force training center, appointing Hu Daonan as the director. The tax revenue from Jiaokeng was to be handed over to the training center for management. Ye Weihai's regiment of Commander Huang's army stationed in Yongding, in cooperation with Hu Daonan, recruited the old Xinan District militia under Zheng Yaochuan and reorganized it into an anti-communist corps, appointing Zheng as the captain. In mid-November, Commander Huang's army was transferred away from Yongding. Zheng, under Ye's orders, was transferred to Jinfeng to await orders. On the 21st of that month, they arrived at Xibian and, due to insufficient supplies, borrowed 30 silver dollars from the Jiaokeng tax collection office. The tax collector, Li Guisan, refused, as the Jiaokeng tax collection office had not handed over management to the training center as per the resolution. Li Guisan and Zheng had a heated argument. Zheng, acting on Hu Daonan's orders, disarmed the militia guarding the tax revenue in Jiaokeng, confiscating six rifles and two pistols, and detaining three tax collectors. Two other tax officials carrying pistols were also disarmed of two pistols by the Zhongkeng militia while they were out. This occurred on the 22nd. Upon hearing of this, Li Yuying was furious. On the 23rd, he led a joint defense force of 70 or 80 men from his and neighboring villages and marched to Xiayang, on the border of Dapu County in Guangdong, and surrounded the headquarters of the Xiayang volunteer corps. The Xiayang volunteer corps retreated to the Zhongkeng volunteer corps headquarters on the mountain top, having been informed in advance by telephone from Xiayang and prepared defenses on the mountain. When Li Yuying arrived at the Xiayang Bridge, both sides immediately opened fire across the stream. Zheng Yaochuan's unit, still in Jiaokeng, heard the gunfire and advanced towards Liyiwuo, sending a squad to attack. Li's forces retreated slightly. Although the original Zhongkeng militia was under Hu Daonan's command, it was divided into three factions at the time, and they shirked responsibility during the battle. Zheng's unit advanced fiercely, while the Zhongkeng militia retreated. The battle ceased at dusk, with Zheng's unit losing a squad leader named Zhang Decai. Both sides suffered casualties. That night, local gentry Chen Yuanhou, Cao Zhifang, Zhang Youtun, and over ten others stepped forward to mediate and reached a resolution: (1) The joint defense force would retrieve the three tax collectors, including Li Guisan, from Jiaokeng. At the same time, the Xiayang market town would be designated as a buffer zone, and both sides would withdraw their troops from Xiayang. (2) The mediators would be responsible for returning the confiscated firearms in Jiaokeng, and the joint defense force would retreat to Hukeng. (3) Both sides would send representatives and impartial individuals to mediate and resolve the matter within a set time frame to prevent the situation from escalating. (4) The tax revenue from Jiaokeng would be handed over to a financial committee composed of local people for public collection and distribution, with neither side interfering. That night, the mediators worked tirelessly throughout the night. At 8:00 AM on the 24th, representatives from all sides gathered at the Xiayang market town. Li Guisan and others were handed over to Su Jingwu, who signed a receipt. After Li was released, Li Yuying's joint defense force did not honor the agreement. They only withdrew the sentries from the Hu clan's ancestral hall and refused to leave Xiayang. They also demanded the return of the confiscated pistols and rifles from the non-confiscated tax officials, refusing to leave. The mediators then withdrew. People in Zhongkeng mostly blamed Hu Daonan for being inexperienced, causing harm to their hometown. Some complained to Li Yuying, revealing Hu's shortcomings. Li was well aware of the complex internal situation of Zhongkeng and that Hu Daonan could not control or command the various militias. On one hand, he sent people to Fuxi to invite Huang Chaigou to lead the Fuxi militia to join the fighting, and also requested troops from the Third Regiment of Nan'an to come to Xiayang to bolster their strength. On the other hand, he declared to the Zhongkeng representatives that Li was only targeting Hu Daonan, and the grievances had specific targets, having nothing to do with the Zhongkeng people and would not cause any trouble. Except for the showdown with Zheng Yaochuan, all other armed militias were considered brothers. Huang Chaigou's unit from Fuxi indeed arrived on the 24th, with extremely untidy uniforms and a mix of old and new weapons. Those carrying bamboo baskets followed behind, in a grand and overwhelming manner, attacking Zhongkeng with all their might. The Zhongkeng militia could not hold out and retreated to Jiaokeng Xibian. Li Yuying attacked Zhongkeng at noon, burning down Hu Daonan's entire building. The entire village was looted, and those carrying bamboo baskets left with full loads. Twelve young women were also kidnapped. Li's forces retreated to Xiayang in the afternoon and detained the kidnapped women in the Zhonghe Building in Taipingzhai. There were reports of gang rape. Yongding natives residing in Dapu County were extremely indignant upon hearing the news and sent Zhang Minquan, Lu Zuoping, and ten others to mediate. They arrived in Xiayang on the 29th and negotiated with Li Yuying to release the twelve women who had been raped and were suffering from illness. They were placed in Zeng Baichuan's house for medical treatment. After the representatives from Dapu arrived, they invited local gentry Liao Haitao, Chen Yuanhou, and Cao Zhifang to mediate again. Zhongkeng paid 600 yuan as compensation for the two confiscated pistols, as a condition for the release of the twelve women. Li demanded an additional 100 yuan to cover losses. While negotiations were underway, Li's forces attacked Zheng Yaochuan in Jiaokeng again, and the second mediation was interrupted. The Zhongkeng faction, having been looted, had united, and both sides fought desperately. The number of casualties is unknown. As of December 2nd.

Inspection Tour of Jiangxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei (Special Correspondent Ren An)

Local Ruffians in Konglong Bully Others and Illegally Collect Boat Taxes

Huangmei Called "Little Tianzhu," People Suffer Great Hardship

Huangmei Correspondence: After returning from Jingfu to Huangchuan, I originally intended to go directly to Lu'an in Anhui via Gushi, or to Lihuang, the newly established county seat in western Anhui, via Shangcheng. However, the roads were difficult to travel. Therefore, I took the original route, returned to Wuhan, and took a riverboat to Xiaochikou, across from Jiujiang, then transferred to a boat to Huangmei and then to western Anhui.

Forty miles north of Xiaochikou lies Konglong. Although it is a small town, it is a transportation hub connecting neighboring areas. People from all walks of life gather here, and personnel disputes occur from time to time. Over the years, no fewer than two or three hundred ships have passed through the town's pier. A group of local ruffians secretly formed a gang, forcibly collecting pier taxes, not for local public expenses, but for the gang's private distribution, with thirty-one shares in total. Those with greater influence, or those who bravely stepped forward due to disputes, could receive two or three shares, or half a share. The members were extremely complex, including fierce old men, widows, young children, and failed scholars, lacking uniformity. The amount of tax collected was also extremely heavy. Regardless of the type of ship, 60% of the business income was taken. The boatmen's hard-earned money was exhausted, leaving them with only 40%. If they concealed any income, the ships that provided their family's livelihood would be in danger of being destroyed. It is truly shocking. In 1928, Huangmei County Magistrate Li Jinfang once banned this practice, but the town's thieving became rampant for a time, especially pickpocketing at the pier. In 1930, the gang resurfaced and established a shipping union, continuing to collect pier taxes, reducing the rate from 60% to 40%. Moreover, the shareholders built eighteen ships to control the shipping industry, giving them priority for all cargo and passenger transport. In recent years, due to droughts, many farmers abandoned farming and engaged in the shipping industry, leading to a sudden increase in sailing ships, reaching more than two hundred. However, due to the loss of business, those who requested to join the union were rejected, leading to growing resentment. A month ago, a wine merchant transported several jars of wine on a civilian ship to Huangmei. The union, claiming a loss of their priority rights, insisted on transferring the wine to their own ship, leading to a dispute and a brawl, severely injuring the ship owner and smashing the wine jars. The merchant filed a complaint with the county government. The county magistrate, considering that the union had too few ships to meet the legal requirements for a union, intended to dissolve it. However, fearing their power, he instead ordered District Chief Wang Kenian to mediate. The union paid five silver dollars to settle the matter. However, the issue of protecting the business of the two hundred civilian ships and banning the heavy taxes was never mentioned. It is rumored that the union secretly sends ten yuan a month from the tax revenue to the Chamber of Commerce, and District Chief Wang, who also serves as the Chamber of Commerce president, is suspected of favoring and helping the evildoers. Now, the two hundred civilian boat owners, unable to withstand the exploitation and the pressure of life, are filled with anger and are about to engage in a life-and-death struggle with the union. The union, with its many unsavory characters, is also eager to fight. It is widely believed that a major disaster is brewing. Once it erupts, it will have a significant negative impact on social order. A spark can ignite a prairie fire, and the interests of the working masses should not be exploited for long. The principle is very clear, and those who govern the people should not ignore it. The county seat is sixty miles from Konglong. The market is still good. Many small peasant landowners live in the countryside, eating coarse food and wearing rough clothes year-round, living a very hard life. In particular, the price of oil and salt is extremely high (salt is 960 cash per catty, equivalent to 6,500 cash in silver), and many people cannot afford to eat it for months. The price of land rose to two or three hundred yuan per dou (unit of measurement) of land between 1926 and 1926, but has now fallen to below one hundred yuan. Wages have also fallen along with the land price. Li Ziying, with the help of various parties, has occupied Pingzhai on the western side of Jiaokeng, and is currently stationed in the Zou surname's enclosed building. Li treats the areas he occupies as conquered territory, and the people are greatly ravaged, with rape and robbery being commonplace. Zheng Yaochuan's forces were defeated and retreated to Yanxia, below Yamatam. Four days later, both sides made contact and the conflict turned into a large-scale clan feud. Li Ziying beheaded a squad leader and a soldier from Zheng's unit and displayed their heads to the public. Li's ferocity is increasing. The Luxi militia in Nan'an County has also recently clashed with Li's forces, due to Luxi cattle dealers leading cattle through Nanxi, which were robbed by Li's forces. Many women from Nanxi who went to Luxi to buy rice were robbed. Both sides gathered crowds across the river for a major battle. The Fujian authorities have no time to attend to both military suppression and pacification, and the Guangdong army cannot easily intervene. It is unknown how this matter will be resolved. (15th)

The price of land fluctuates from time to time. People still value the town and do not easily sell their property. In recent years, due to continuous famines, income is insufficient, and the trend of selling land is gradually increasing. This can be seen in the sales contracts. Moreover, there is a superstitious system of dividing property, and some people only sell property after a son dies. For example, if there are six dou of land and three sons, and one son dies, they must sell the two dou that the deceased son should have received to pay for funeral expenses. There is no deposit for renting land, but the annual rent must be paid in advance in the previous year. If the rent is not paid in the previous year or is overdue, interest will be charged at 30% per annum on the outstanding rent.

The county is divided into four districts, each with nine towns. The joint defense funds for each district are added to the land tax. There are six security teams, which require annual expenses of 110,000 to 120,000 yuan. It is said that many district chiefs are corrupt. There are very few bandits being caught, and the people cannot bear the burden. They have repeatedly requested a reduction in the teams, but their requests have not been approved. The people are resentful. There are more than ten miscellaneous taxes, with the bandit suppression levy being the heaviest. The people are required to pay 40 yuan per person to hire laborers, which has now risen to 100 yuan, and there are no people willing to be hired. Beggars are prevalent in the four rural areas, and beggars are not ashamed. There are three reasons for this: (1) The area is the birthplace of the Fourth Patriarch Daoxin, the Fifth Patriarch Hongren, and the Sixth Patriarch Huineng, and is known as "Little Tianzhu." The so-called Buddhist sites of the Fourth Patriarch Mountain, Fifth Patriarch Mountain, and the Eastern Zen Temple, where the Sixth Patriarch practiced, as well as the Fifth Patriarch Temple seen on the way to Susong, are serene and solemn with various ancestral relics. Tens of thousands of devout men and women from various provinces travel thousands of miles to worship Buddha every year. The villagers used to receive alms and became accustomed to it. After 1930, the incense at the temples declined sharply, and no one gave alms, feeling like they had lost their jobs. (2) The terrain is low and humid, with many lakes and rivers. The rivers are easily flooded and silted up, leading to frequent disasters and no means of survival. (3) Gambling is rampant, with organizations called "Brotherhood Societies" engaging in gambling every day. If it is in the city or town, they are still cautious and set up secret gambling dens. In the countryside, they openly entice villagers to gamble all day and night, resulting in the gamblers losing their fortunes and livelihoods. Families of several people are forced to become beggars. In addition, there is a type of begging where poor farmers leave only one or two family members to guard the house after the harvest, and the rest go begging in other places, some even going directly to Wuhan and returning after several months. Some say it is a custom, but it is actually due to insufficient food, forcing them to do so.

Jiangsu Province Decides to Change Administrative Regions

Five Commissioners to be Established in Jiangbei

All Districts in Jiangnan to be Abolished

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Jiangsu provincial authorities have recently decided to increase the powers of the administrative commissioners, who will no longer concurrently hold the position of county magistrate. All districts in Jiangnan will be abolished. In Jiangbei, including Yangzhong and Chongming in the center of the Yangtze River, five districts will be established. It is reported that the counties under the jurisdiction of the five districts are as follows: District 1: Jiangdu, Yizheng, Liuhe, Jiangpu, Yangzhong, Gaoyou, Baoying, Taixian; District 2: Nantong, Rugao, Jingjiang, Haimen, Taixing, Dongtai, Qidong, Chongming; District 3: Huai'an, Huaiyin, Siyang, Lianshui, Funing, Yancheng, Xinghua; District 4: Tongshan, Fengxian, Peixian, Xiaoxian, Dangshan, Pizhou; District 5: Donghai, Suqian, Suining, Guanyun, Shuyang, Ganyu. The above are a total of thirty-five counties, and the distribution of their districts is roughly as such. There may be temporary changes. As for the reason for abolishing the Jiangnan commissioners, it is believed that Jiangnan has convenient transportation and is more peaceful than Jiangbei, and its area is not as large as Jiangbei. Therefore, it is not necessary to establish commissioners to promote autonomy in Jiangnan. It is also understood that Jiangbei is taking self-defense measures, and the abolition of district chiefs and the implementation of the baojia system may be implemented together. As for the selection of commissioners, it is said that those with military knowledge and political acumen are qualified and are currently being reviewed.

Qingpu

Four Bandits Arrested in a Small Inn

On the night of the 23rd, the Huangdu Jiajie Sixth District Security Corps arrested four people from Taizhou, Xu A'er, Zhao Baotai, Huang A'er, and Gu A'er, at the Gaosheng Inn in this town. They were immediately taken back to the Corps headquarters. According to their confessions, they had robbed the boss Shen Fu'an three times near Huangdu last month, shared the stolen money, and hid in Shanghai. They had more than twenty accomplices and a pistol and a Mauser pistol. They said that they were avoiding the limelight, Shen told us to temporarily hide at a friend's place who is a cobbler in Huangdu, and someone would come to lead us tomorrow morning, so we stayed at the inn and were arrested. Today, the victims, Mao Zhengshan and others from Xiwancun in this county, identified that Xu and others had robbed their house. Chief Jin immediately prepared a document and escorted them to the county government for legal action.

Songjiang

Prosecution in the Case of Pushing Someone into the Sea

Due to the purchase of fish caught by fishermen, Jiang Zhengxing Fish Shop in Jinshanwei was undercut by Jiang Zhengji Fish Shop owner Jiang Xiaomei, leading to a dispute. Jiang Xiaomei lured Jiang Zhouwang and his brother, the owners of Jiang Zhengxing Fish Shop, and violently pushed them into the sea out of spite. Jiang Zhouwang and his brothers drank seawater until their voices were hoarse. Their appetite has decreased significantly recently, indicating internal injuries. They are truly unwilling to accept this, so Jiang Zhouwang and his brothers filed a lawsuit in the Songjiang County Court Prosecutor's Office against Jiang Xiaomei for attempted murder to uphold justice.

Verdict in the Lawsuit over the Site of the Provincial Experimental Elementary School

The site of the Provincial Experimental Elementary School next to the Songwei Road was involved in a lawsuit with the local resident Zhang Jiecai over land rights. The case was initially judged by the county court, and Zhang Jiecai appealed. The higher court sent the case back to the county for retrial. The county court has now issued a judgment stating that in the lawsuit between Zhang Jiecai and Shen Shoujin over the land, Shen Shoujin shall return to Zhang Jiecai seven fen and nine li of Huangzi Weiji Tian in Fangyi Tu. The litigation costs shall be borne by Shen Shoujin.

Nantong

Seventh District to Conduct Village Clearing

The Seventh District, consisting of five counties, Nantong, Rugao, Haimen, Qidong, and Chongming, is plagued by lurking bandits and roaming soldiers. After discussions between representatives of the military, government, and police organs of each county, it was decided to conduct village clearing. The commissioner of the Seventh District drafted a plan and submitted it to the province for approval. It has now been approved to organize village clearing teams. A Village Clearing Headquarters will be established in the Commissioner's Office to direct the operation, which is scheduled to be completed in one month.

Suzhou

Abuses Arise from Lifting the Ban on Cattle Slaughter

The Wuxian Business Tax Collection Bureau, under orders to collect cattle slaughter taxes, opened slaughtering yesterday (the 26th). All ten cattle slaughter licenses have been obtained by cattle merchants Ma Changrong and others from the Bureau. Another group of cattle merchants, Cheng Shutang and five others, argued that the Bureau's issuance of licenses was not announced in advance and was completely done in private, so that genuine cattle merchants did not receive licenses. They pointed out that five of the ten people who received licenses were not cattle merchants and were manipulating the slaughtering to profit from it, causing genuine cattle merchants to be forced to close down and their livelihoods to be disrupted. They submitted a petition yesterday (the 26th) to the Business Tax Bureau and the Suzhou Finance Department, requesting assistance.

Wuxi

Septuagenarian Dies in Fire

Lu A'tu, a villager from Liannuoqiao in Yangming Township, was over seventy years old and a stonemason by trade. He had four sons, all of whom lived separately from their father due to disagreements. A'tu built several thatched houses for himself to shelter from the wind and rain. The day before yesterday, in the evening, A'tu dumped the hot ash from the foot stove into a bamboo sieve. The ash had not been completely extinguished, and in the middle of the night, it caught fire, and the fierce flames were unstoppable. The thatched houses were completely burned down. A'tu, due to his old age, could not escape and was burned to death. It was truly tragic.

Changzhou

Planning Two New Urban Areas

Wu County Magistrate Cai Pei recently planned two new urban areas in the northeast and southwest to improve the city's appearance. All plans were submitted to the County Council on the 25th and passed. The northeastern new urban area is located in the northeast of the city, north of Northeast Main Street, near the North Gate Guanhe Road. The southwestern new urban area is located in the southwest of the city, south of Huaide Bridge to the east, including the Carpenter Street south of the South Gate to the west bank of the South New Canal. This western area has recently been building roads, and the market is becoming increasingly prosperous. It is planned to first send personnel to survey the detailed terrain, determine the location and width of the streets, as well as the location of public wells, public toilets, fire stations, and other public facilities, and select a site for a public park. The county administrative meeting has approved this, and it must be actively carried out according to the plan.

Three Arrested in Robbery and Assault Case

The home of Zhang Yaoxi in Anning Township, the 16th district of Wu County, was robbed and the owner was injured on the 17th of this month. The case was serious. District Chief Xie Jun of the district tried to gather information and help with the arrest. He learned that fugitives were hiding in Donggu Village, Gubian Township, and secretly sent police and militia to the village. They arrested Yu Quansheng, Ding Fusheng, and Ding Longda, who were suspects in the case. During the preliminary interrogation, Yu Quansheng confessed to participating in the robbery of the Zhang family, saying that there were six people in total, with two guns and a single knife. Ding Fusheng and Ding Longda have not yet provided a clear confession. District Chief Xie escorted the three criminals to the county yesterday (the 25th) for interrogation.

Female Workers of a Silk Factory Sit-in to Demand Wages

Yao Jincheng, the manager of Wanfengtai Tobacco Shop in Xiyingli, Wu County, made a profit of over 10,000 yuan from selling silkworm cocoons this spring. He then rented a closed silk factory in Xi and opened for business under the name Qingfeng, employing over 2,000 female workers. However, the silk market fell sharply shortly after opening, leading to losses. Over 10,000 yuan in wages were owed to all staff and female workers, with the female workers accounting for about 6,000 to 7,000 yuan. The female workers, because the factory has been closed for several months and their wages have not been paid, sent over seventy representatives, all wearing the factory badge, to Changzhou from Xi by car around 4:00 PM on the 25th to sit-in at Wanfengtai. As of the evening, there was no solution.

Zhenjiang

Water Police Crack Kidnapping Case

Zhang Bao'san, a resident of Tianxin Bridge in Taixing, had a comfortable family life. In the late night of the 18th of this month, eight bandits suddenly broke into his house with guns and kidnapped Zhang and his four-year-old child to a boat that was waiting nearby. They sailed to the Sanjiangying area. Just as the Ningkou ferry was releasing steam, Zhang heard the sound in the boat and knew he was near the dock. He bravely drew a knife and jumped into the river. The water police on the ferry noticed the person who jumped into the river was bound by ropes, and knew that there must be bandits on the boat. They ordered the boat to stop and arrested five bandits, Gu Shuren and others, on the boat. Zhang Bao'san, the kidnapped victim who jumped into the river, was also rescued. Three other bandits escaped with a small kidnapped victim in a small boat. The bandits were taken to the Bajiaokou team headquarters. After interrogation by Captain Gao Maoting, they confessed. They were escorted to the Guazhou district headquarters for interrogation yesterday.

Jiangyin

Disturbance at the Song Family Elementary School

The Song Family Elementary School in Changjing Town, the 12th district, was founded by the merchants Song Chuying and Song Cucai, using the Song family ancestral hall as the school building. It has been around for fourteen years, and the number of graduates is no less than three hundred. The school's auditorium is usually used as a staff room and reception room, so it is luxuriously decorated and neatly organized. There are no less than one hundred kinds of forms, mirrors, books, and furnishings on the four walls. However, at 10:30 AM yesterday, during the winter solstice, when the school's third class was about to end, two people suddenly broke into the auditorium. At that time, there were six teachers in the school, four of whom were teaching, and only two were working at their desks. They were shocked. Unexpectedly, the intruders destroyed all the items. At this time, the bell rang to end the class, and the two hundred children in the four classrooms suddenly heard a loud noise and screamed and ran in all directions. Later, the outside world learned about it, and spectators came in droves. Rumors spread in the market, causing a great stir. On the north-south streets and east-west markets, people were either shocked by the riot or suspected robbery. The situation was chaotic for a while. Fortunately, District Chief Wang of the 12th district and Inspector Hu of the Education Bureau happened to be in Chang on business and went to the school to investigate. However, the perpetrators had already fled. After detailed investigation, it was learned that the two were Song Zhonglu and Song Zhongli, graduates of the school. Inspector Hu summoned the two and rebuked them, and then summoned the children, persuaded them to start classes, and reported to the Bureau Chief, strictly demanding impeachment. But it is unknown when the disturbance will subside.

Water Police Intercept Bandit Ticket

Xu Wenquan, a patrol officer of the Second Squad of the 15th Brigade of the Water Public Security in Bajiaokou, the fourth district of the county, led police officers on a patrol along the river on the morning of the 25th. Father and Son Fight, Resulting in Homicide

Tang Xinli, a villager from Tangjiaji Township in Yiling, was sixty-one years old. He had four sons. Due to discord with his family, he had previously taken his wife and children to rent a house elsewhere. Now, due to the difficulty of maintaining a living, he intended to move back to the old house and discussed it with his father, but did not get his consent. Disputes Arise Frequently Between Tenants and Landlords Due to Excessive Water Bills

Ken Yie Denies Collecting Fees from Residents for Well Drilling

The Trial of the Case of the Three Lane Neighborhoods of Bai Fu, etc. is Postponed for Retrial

Since Tonghai Lane, Tongzhou Road, Hongkou, had its water cut off by the British Shanghai Waterworks Company on the 19th of this month, as a result of appeals from all parties and consultations, the water was immediately turned on. According to reports the day before yesterday, the landlord intended to seek a permanent solution by drilling an artesian well and charging each resident a special fee of twenty yuan. Yesterday, the Ken Yie Bank Real Estate Department, the landlord of the lane, denied this. The lawsuit involving the three lane neighborhoods of Bai Fu, Bai Lu, and Bai Shou due to the water bill issue was heard again yesterday, but no results were obtained. The details are as follows:

Collection of Fees for Well Drilling is Inaccurate: The Ken Yie Bank Real Estate Department issued a statement yesterday saying, "The report on the 24th of this month said that the water cut-off in Tonghai Lane, Tongzhou Road, Hongkou, has been resolved, and the landlord collected a special fee of twenty-one yuan from the tenants to drill an artesian well. This is slightly different from the facts. The water bill of the lane is very high. In addition to paying the water bill, the landlord asked the tenants to subsidize a small amount, but no results were obtained. After many days of delay, the water was cut off. This was entirely initiated by the British Shanghai Waterworks Company. Although the water pipes have been temporarily reconnected after appeals from all parties, the right to turn on and off the water still depends on whether the water bill is paid. However, after careful examination of the company's letter, it is required that the arrears be settled by the end of this month. Therefore, it is difficult to guarantee that the water will not be cut off again in the future. As for the rent increase, it is absolutely not intended in this time of economic depression. We hope for correction."

Advise Tenants to Cooperate: The Ken Yie Bank, the landlord of Tonghai Lane, issued a notice to the residents and landlords of the lane yesterday, saying, "Since we started managing this lane, we have been on good terms with the residents for several years. Unexpectedly, in December of last year, the British Shanghai Waterworks Company unilaterally cancelled the water package system and installed water meters, resulting in monthly water bills that exceeded the previous bill by two times. Who can afford it in this time of economic depression? And recently, the sudden water cut-off has caused great inconvenience to the residents. Although we have made efforts to appeal, we have only obtained a moment of peace. However, water is essential for life and the demand is urgent. We have repeatedly sent

instructions and have sent special commissioners three times to sincerely negotiate and subsidize the huge water bills used by the residents so that the landlords can afford it. This is to bring the two sides closer and succeed. If the residents do not recognize the water bill at all, how can the landlords afford to pay the full amount? It will inevitably be delayed and there will be no solution. Then, the water cut-off in the future is not far away. At that time, both sides will be injured and the pain will be great. We hope that the residents will not ignore our words, and we have high hopes for that."

Lawsuit Involving the Lane Neighborhoods of Bai Fu, etc.: After the three lane neighborhoods of Bai Fu, Bai Lu, and Bai Shou between Pingliang Road and Fenzhou Road in eastern Shanghai changed to the water meter system, the water bill increased by three to four times, making it difficult for the landlords to afford it. They refused to pay the water bill, and the water was cut off once in May of this year. Then, it was also postponed and opened as a temporary solution. Afterwards, when the Deli Company, the landlord of the lane, dug an artesian well, the water company found out and cut off the water pipe of the temporary emergency source in the late last month. The tenants did not understand the difficulties of the landlord and thought that it was intentionally delayed. Therefore, they specially hired a lawyer to issue a warning, put forward four conditions, and demanded compensation for the loss. The landlord strongly rejected it. Therefore, they could not get any results and filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court. After the court session on the 19th, the tenants' association organized by the tenants was deemed to be an illegal group because it had not been approved by the party and government authorities. Immediately, more than 190 representatives were elected to file another lawsuit with the First Special District Court under their joint names. The sixth court session was held on the day before yesterday (the 25th). After a brief trial of the plaintiff and defendant, it was deemed that the facts were not clear and witnesses were to be summoned. The trial was rescheduled to January 11. At that time, Kui Yanfang, the chairman of the Real Estate Association, must also be present to testify.

The Thousand Yuan Silver Bar Policy

Only Suitable for Clearing Among the Trade

Private Transfer is Not Allowed

——Decision to Issue on New Year's Day——

The Shanghai Mint, in order to facilitate the circulation of existing currency in the financial community, has decided to cast silver bars in two types, A and B, each worth one thousand yuan, to replace existing cash. It has already officially started casting and is scheduled to be officially issued from January 1, 1934. However, it is only suitable for clearing among the trade and private transfer is not allowed. Yesterday, a notice was issued to the Silver and Money Trade Associations that they should be universally used. The text of the circular is as follows: "This is to inform you that we have received Instruction No. 1600 from the Ministry of Finance, which states, 'Article 12 of the Amended Regulations on the Casting of Silver Standard Coins states that the Central Mint may cast factory bars in two types, A and B. Type A weighs 23.493448 grams, with a fineness of 999 per thousand. Type B weighs 26.697.1 grams, with 880 parts silver and 120 parts copper, equivalent to one thousand silver standard coins, all marked on their face.' The Ministry has announced and implemented it, and the Ministry has approved the styles of the two types of factory bars and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government for record, and ordered the Central Mint to cast them. It is now scheduled that the two types of factory bars, A and B, will be issued on January 1, 1934, to meet the needs of the market. However, Type B factory bars were originally intended to facilitate the collection and distribution among members of the silver and money industry and are not applicable to private transfers, in order to show restrictions. In addition to separately announcing and sending letters, we hereby order the Association to inform and transfer to all members to comply with. The Type B factory bars shall not be used outside of collection and distribution among members of the industry. All banks and money houses must strictly comply with and not exceed the restrictions, otherwise, they will be punished. We hereby inform you.' We hereby record and announce it for your reference. Shanghai Money Trade Association, December 26, 1933."

The Hengshan Steamer of the Sanbei Shipping Company Runs into Trouble

Collided with a Ship in Zhenjiang

Ran Aground in Nanjing

The Hengshan steamer of the Sanbei Shipping Company, which sailed to Nanjing on the 23rd of this month, had a tragic accident of sinking a small ship when it arrived in Zhenjiang, and ran aground when it arrived in Nanjing. It can be said that misfortunes never come singly. The details are as follows:

Transporting Oil to Zhenjiang: The Chongshan ship usually sails to various ports in the north and south. Recently, it has picked up a large batch of kerosene and machine oil from the Dexijie Foreign Company in this port, which will be loaded and unloaded in Zhenjiang and Nanjing. The ship arrived in Zhenjiang first on the 23rd and stopped at the Dexigu Wharf for unloading.

Colliding with a Large Sand Boat: At 6:05 AM on the 24th, the Hengshan ship arrived in Zhenjiang and stopped at the Dexigu Wharf. When it was mooring, a large sand boat loaded with cargo, named Dingsheng, was sailing upstream. When the Hengshan ship was turning, it could not avoid the collision (according to the shipowner's report), so it crashed into the sand boat. The Dingsheng ship was hit and immediately destroyed. The ship sank into the river, and all the boatmen on board fell into the water. After the accident, the owner of the Hengshan ship quickly released sampan boats and lifebuoys into the water to rescue the people who fell into the water. Another sand boat also heard the alarm and rushed to help.

Ships and Goods Were Destroyed: The Zhenjiang Customs small steamboat received the alarm and flew to the vicinity of the Dexigu Wharf to coordinate with various small boats to rescue the people who fell into the water. The Dingsheng ship and the goods loaded on it have all sunk into the river. The boatmen in the ship were mostly rescued. The sand boat and its cargo suffered great losses. The Zhenjiang Customs small boat is now handling the rescue matters. As for the issue of liability for the accident, both parties must be interrogated before the right and wrong can be determined.

Ranged Aground Again in Nanjing: After this incident, the shipowner has reported to Shanghai by telegram yesterday afternoon. Then, after unloading all the goods in Zhenjiang, it sailed to Nanjing. Yesterday morning, when the ship was about to arrive at the Nanjing Wharf, it ran aground on the shallow water of the river bank again in order to avoid a small naval boat on the river surface. The ship lost its ability to move, and the goods in the ship could not be unloaded. The shipowner sent a telegram to Shanghai to report and asked the Nanjing Sanbei Branch to send a boat to rescue. After several hours, the small boat sent by the Nanjing Branch was able to pull the ship out of the shoal with great effort during high tide in the afternoon. Yesterday afternoon, a telegram had arrived in Shanghai. After the ship collided and ran aground, it is still necessary to return to Shanghai for inspection to determine whether the hull was damaged.

The Zhabei Charitable Organizations Sent a Letter to the Xinwei Relief Association

The Closure of Silk Factories Has Led to a Sudden Increase in Labor Unemployment

Plan to Set Up a Congee Kitchen and Request Funding Assistance

Zhabei was originally a prosperous industrial and commercial area. It was hit hard by the January 28 Incident. In recent months, due to the sharp drop in silk prices, silk factories have closed down one after another, resulting in a sudden increase in labor unemployment. They wander in the streets day and night, exposed to the wind and dew, unable to make a living. In view of this, Zhabei charitable organizations plan to set up a congee kitchen to provide relief. Therefore, yesterday, Wang Binyan, the director of the organization, sent a letter to the Xinwei Relief Association. The original text is as follows: "Zhabei is always crowded with poor people every winter. Our organization has always opened factories to distribute congee. Many old, weak, women, and children go to the factory to eat. A bowl of hot congee is enough to extend their lives. After Zhabei was hit by the war last spring, the local economy has not recovered, and the market is depressed. Many silk factories have closed down due to the sharp drop in prices, and labor unemployment is on the rise. In addition, the rural economy is bankrupt, and there are more poor people than before. In this severe winter weather, they are hungry and cold and cannot survive. The situation is very pitiful. Therefore, this winter, we have to open a congee kitchen (at the Second Congee Kitchen on Liuying Road). To prevent freezing, we ordered craftsmen to repair it as soon as possible to save the general poor people. However, once it is opened, the cost is more than 10,000 or 20,000 yuan. Although some philanthropists have donated recently, it is rare. Last year, we received enthusiastic assistance from your organization, which was enough to provide relief. In view of the current situation of the poor people this winter, we have to ask for your relief and assistance to open the factory as before. Please also widely solicit donations from your organization, so that we can get a steady stream of money and rice to provide relief, so that most of the poor people can be grateful for their rebirth and share the benevolent soup. We are sincerely looking forward to it."

The Social Bureau is Ordered to Stop the Incorporation of Various Industries Under Assumed Names

Careful Assessment Should Be Conducted During the Preparation Stage

The Social Bureau instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, saying, "According to Instruction No. 7855 of the Municipal Government, it is forwarded that according to Consultation No. 21537 from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation submitted a request to stop establishing trade unions under false pretenses in order to avoid disputes. This case is the same as the Ministry's previous general plan to unify the names of trade unions in various places and industries. In addition to sending a letter to the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee and approving the Chamber of Commerce Federation, a copy of the original submission is sent to your bureau for reference and to instruct the Social Bureau to carefully assess and examine the trade unions that apply for preparation in the future in order to avoid disputes. The original submission is attached. With this approval, we order you to send a copy of the original attachment to the Association for compliance and to instruct all affiliated trade unions to comply with. This is the order." The following is an appendix to the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation's submission to the Ministry (omitted above): "The Second Meeting of the Current General Assembly of our Association approved the proposal of the Yilin Town Chamber of Commerce, which stated that the organization of trade unions is based on the Trade Union Law, and there is no problem. Unexpectedly, the organizers do not handle matters in accordance with the law. For example, the grocery industry is renamed the South Goods Industry, a guild has already been established in the same industry, but the timber industry is also organized, and a guild has already been established in the same grain industry, but the soybean, wheat, and rice industry is also organized. The purpose is to create opposition at the beginning and gradually start disputes at the end. We should ask the party and government organs of each county to carefully assess and examine the trade unions that apply for preparation in order to avoid disputes and benefit commerce. It was immediately submitted to the General Assembly for discussion, and it was agreed that this case should be approved as it is and instructed the party and government organs of each county to carefully assess and examine the trade unions that apply for preparation in order to prevent abuses. The resolution was unanimously passed and recorded in the minutes. We hereby submit a document for your approval and allow its implementation, which is for the public convenience. Sincerely submitted."

Fundraising Measures for the Hotel Industry

Wu Tiecheng Invited Representatives of the Industry to Discuss

Wu Tiecheng, the captain of the Chinese Aviation Association's Fundraising Corps, specially hosted a banquet at the Bankers' Association Club yesterday afternoon to discuss the collection of aviation patriotic donations by the hotel industry in this city, inviting the Standing Committee of the Municipal Hotel Industry Association and representatives of hotels that have not joined the Association. It was agreed that the Association would determine the date and inform the industry to start collecting, and the Municipal Government would notify the hotels that have not joined the Association to implement it. The details are as follows:

Invite Discussion: When the Chinese Aviation Association started raising donations in the spring of this year, the hotel industry in this city pledged to donate 200,000 yuan. At that time, the Association drafted ten measures for the hotel industry in Shanghai to collect aviation patriotic donations and reported them to the Municipal Government, which were forwarded to the Hotel Industry Association for implementation. However, because there are still some hotels in this city that have not joined the Association, although hotels that have not joined the Association have been convened to participate in the discussion, no decision has been made on the measures. In order to implement it as soon as possible, Captain Wu Tiecheng specially set up a banquet at the Bankers' Association Club yesterday with Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to invite people from the industry to discuss the measures.

Meeting Situation: The representatives who attended the banquet yesterday included Zou Juncheng, the representative of the Association, and the representatives of various hotels: Lu Liankui, Sun Qiuping (Asia), Gao Weifu (Meng Yuan), Xu Chunxiang (Yipinxiang China), Xie Jiantang (Lao Dingsheng), Zhao Quansheng (Dajiangnan), Dong Zhenlong, Shen Changgeng (Central), Wu Duansheng (Nanjing), Li Wencai (Zhongnan), Xu Wenzhao (Hongfu), Yao Zhaoji (Chunjiang), Zhou Songxi (Hygiene), and representatives of the Aviation Association: Lin Wojiang, officials of the Fundraising Corps Office: Li Dachao, Zhou Nianxing, Zhang Yuliang, etc. During the meeting, it was decided that the Hotel Industry Association would convene a meeting to pass the principles and measures for collecting aviation donations, notify the Aviation Association, and forward them to the Municipal Government to notify the hotels that have not joined the Association. Then, a general meeting will be convened to determine the date of commencement of collection. It is heard that the three major hotels in this city, Dadong, Xin Xin, and Dongya, have already started collecting according to the measures set by the Aviation Association on July 1, and have collected 4,000 to 5,000 yuan so far.

Collection Measures: The measures for the hotel industry in Shanghai to collect aviation patriotic donations are recorded as follows: (1) The Chinese Aviation Association has formulated these measures for the purpose of raising aviation patriotic funds. (2) Each hotel shall add a 0.5% (5%) aviation patriotic donation to the room rate. (3) Each hotel shall pay the aviation patriotic donations collected to the Chinese Aviation Association once a week. (4) Each hotel shall issue a receipt for the aviation patriotic donations collected to the passenger. (5) Each hotel shall post the measures for collecting aviation patriotic donations in each room for passengers to read. (6) The hotel industry shall collect aviation patriotic donations for a period of six months. (7) The Chinese Aviation Association shall print a three-part receipt for the aviation patriotic donations collected by the hotel industry and distribute them to each hotel. (8) The Chinese Aviation Association may send personnel to inspect the collection of donations. If there are any abuses, they shall be punished according to law. (9) The Chinese Aviation Association shall publish the amount of aviation patriotic donations collected by the hotel industry every month. (10) These measures shall be submitted to the government for approval and implementation.

The Japanese Expel Overseas Chinese on a Large Scale

A certain vessel returned to Shanghai the previous day and arrived in Shanghai yesterday, looking extremely disheveled. According to reports, Chinese residing in Japan who are engaged in small businesses or work as laborers, even if they have existing jobs, are not allowed to stay because it is said that they are taking away the livelihood of the Japanese. In the past year, no fewer than two or three thousand overseas Chinese from various places have been expelled and returned to their home country. The number of Chinese currently remaining in Japan is less than one-tenth of what it was before. Japanese police are still searching everywhere, and it seems that they will not stop until they have completely expelled all of them.
