Prosperous First Anniversary of the New Huan School

The New Huan School on Parker Road in this city held its first anniversary celebration yesterday and published a special commemorative issue, with the title inscribed by the chairman of the school board, Jiang Wenyu. It includes inscriptions by Mayor Wu, Director Pan, Wu Xingya, Lin Kanghou, Wang Boqun, Ou Yuanhuai, Zheng Tonghe, Chen Xuanshan, Pan Yangyao, Wang Xiaoying, etc., a preface by Cheng Shihui, and various rules, regulations, overviews, reports, plans, outlines, etc. of the school, which are quite complete. At the same time, an achievement exhibition was held, divided into five major rooms: Language Arts, Social Studies, Natural Sciences, Art, and Kindergarten. The school was founded not long ago, but its achievements are remarkable and amazing. The number of visitors reached seven or eight hundred, who all praised it. The anniversary meeting was held at 10 a.m., and Jiang Wenyu, Wang Xiaoying, and other school board members, guests Xu Gongjian, Xu Zehua, etc., and all the staff and students, a total of more than 200 people, attended the meeting. After the ceremonial proceedings, Principal Zhang Zhonghuan delivered a speech, reporting on the past overview, the current general situation, and future plans. School board members Jiang Wenyu and Wang Xiaoying, and guests Xu Gongjian and Xu Zehua, gave speeches and instructions, all of which praised the school. Finally, student representative Wei Ke delivered a speech, and the meeting adjourned at 12 p.m. In the afternoon, the Ningbo Kaixiang Association held a parent-teacher appreciation and entertainment party. First, Principal Zhang Zhonghuan reported, followed by speeches by Director Pan Gong, School Board Members Jiang Wenyu and Pan Yangyao, and then entertainment performances. The audience reached more than 2,000 people, and the event ended after 12 p.m. The entertainment program is recorded as follows, including harmonica ensemble, The Sun Sets, Sad Autumn, Butterfly Girl, Peach Blossom River, Welcoming Spring Song, A Slight Gamble, and A Patriotic Heart, etc.

Soochow Law School Invites French Doctor Bao Dao to Lecture

Soochow Law School held its sixth academic lecture on the evening of the 23rd of this month, with French jurist Dr. Bao Dao as the speaker, entitled "The Internationalization of Criminal Law." His intention was roughly divided into four sections: (1) The purpose of the internationalization of criminal law, (2) The importance of the internationalization of criminal law, (3) The organization of the internationalization of criminal law, as an important part of international conferences, which has undergone four stages of changes to form today's situation, (4) The future efforts that should be made in the internationalization of criminal law, with extensive references and detailed details. The audience was moved. Dr. Bao is a famous jurist in continental Europe who has served as a legal advisor to the National Government for more than 20 years and has made many contributions to the reform of our national criminal law. It is reported that the full text of his speech will be published in the seventh volume, fourth issue of the law journal published by the school.

The Lianglu Football Team Won Its First Battle in the A Group

The A group lost to the Lingnan team by a score of 6 to 5

The B group lost badly by a score of 0 to 5

The Lianglu Football Team played its first game since its establishment yesterday at the Chinese Football Field. The opponent was the Lingnan Team. Both sides were divided into A and B groups and played successively. Starting at 2 p.m., the B group game started first. After the contact, the difference was immediately determined. Because the players in the B group of Lianglu team did too little practice on weekdays, they fought on their own and had no contact. In particular, those who were in charge of the forwards were not good at running, which was a fatal injury. Therefore, as a result, the ratio became 5 to 0, and the Lianglu team suffered a crushing defeat. At 3 o'clock, the two sides changed to the A group team and restarted the game. The players in the A group of the Lianglu team were all veterans who had been fighting on the battlefield for a long time and had a good reputation. Their skills were agile and extraordinary. At the beginning of the game, they took the offensive, so the ball often hovered in front of the Lingnan team's goal. In the first half, they scored four goals and lost only one goal. Unexpectedly, in the second half, their strength was greatly reduced, so they retreated to the defensive position, and lost four goals in a row. Later, they desperately counterattacked and scored two goals. Therefore, the final result was 6 to 5, and the Lianglu team won.

Guanglu Cup Junior Football Competition: Yellow Black Champions, Qiqiao Jia Runners-Up

The Shanghai Pudong Guanglu Sports Association, considering that junior football in Pudong was not as prevalent as in Punan and Puxi, after the conclusion of the Puxi competitions, Gu Zhigao, Wang Zelin, Gu Zhiying, Cao Yulin, and others initiated the Guanglu Cup competition, soliciting participation from various football teams in Pudong. This was purely for promotional purposes, with no fees charged. The competition has been ongoing for over two months, and the finalists were Yellow Black and Qiqiao Jia. Yellow Black brought together junior football stars such as Huang Guorong, Fu Zhibin, Weng Kefa, Wu Jiugao, and others, forming a strong team. Qiqiao Jia was a disguised version of the Qixing team, the champion of the Puxi junior football competition. The two sides were evenly matched, and the final was held at 2:00 PM on the 24th, with referee Mr. Shun Zhigao. The match was full of exciting moments, with spectators frequently cheering. In the end, Yellow Black defeated Qiqiao Jia by a score of 4 to 3, winning the Guanglu Cup presented by the Guanglu Sports Association. The runner-up prize, a silver shield, was personally presented by Mr. Cao Yulin, an official of Guanglu, on the spot. The guests and hosts dispersed in joy.

Spring and Autumn

Prospering the Market

— Xu Xiaoting

Floods, droughts, trampling on agriculture, since the bankruptcy of the rural economy in our country, the provinces and counties in the interior, due to the depression of commerce and sluggish business, the market is poor and deserted. Even the most prosperous and flourishing thoroughfares of the past have, in the blink of an eye, become sparsely populated and filled with death. Under this abnormal development where large cities in the country are becoming more and more developed, and small cities in the interior are becoming more and more squeezed, the society in the interior is like a person who has lost his soul, a rigid situation. The deathly atmosphere of society is already filling the upper layers of the city streets, not just on the ground.

The prosperity of large cities includes cinemas, dance halls, public prostitutes, private prostitutes, and other waiting places, dens for seeking entertainment. Bureaucrats, politicians, and capitalists attract all kinds of people. Cities in the interior fundamentally do not have such beautiful constructions. Once they become deserted, it is like a terminally ill patient with lung disease. Although there is a need to find ways to treat and save them, there is no appropriate method.

Generally, enlightened gentlemen and commercial giants who are worried about the depression of commerce are earnestly and sincerely exploring and researching plans to revitalize the market in order to save this stubborn trend. However, exploration is only exploration. The coldness of the market, all the crowds, are still falling into the abyss of decline, struggling, sighing, and unable to find a ray of hope!

Those who advocate superstition take this situation to launch god-welcoming festivals and perform plays to thank the gods in order to attract the attention of the public and give society a shot in the arm. Friends who hope for commercial development hold big sales and create prize-giving shopping methods in order to stimulate people's purchasing power and compensate for their own business failures. As a result, soap bubbles played by children can only be enjoyed for a while. After this period, they still embark on a miserable path of coldness, decline, and failure!

Since the inland society takes commercial development as the center of market prosperity, and now the commerce of each county is generally showing a downturn, it is really not an easy task for us to demand that a dead society embark on the road to prosperity today. Generally, enlightened people who are worried about the times, although holding twelve points of enthusiasm, try to transform and remedy, and stubbornly want to dig out brilliant gold mines on the surface soil, but this matter is like a dark and cloudy morning, stubbornly hoping for the arrival of sunlight, which is absolutely impossible.

Understanding of Dealing with the World

— Holding Buddha

This golden rule of knowledge is more precious than any knowledge and is not easy to graduate from. Friends who are successful and wealthy have sufficient mastery of this knowledge and have already obtained a diploma. Friends who are frustrated and unsuccessful have no understanding of this knowledge at all. Because there are few people with mastery and many people without understanding, there are few successful and wealthy people in the world and many frustrated and unsuccessful people.

In the ocean, a big fish can swallow hundreds of small fish in one bite. Everyone is a fish, all are equal, why can big fish eat small fish? Big fish and small fish can breathe freely and swim freely in the sea. Why do small fish never shout "injustice" when they are eaten by big fish? What good fortune does the big fish have, what crime does the small fish have? When we deal with the world and have this "understanding," we don't have to complain.

Friends with unyielding integrity are unwilling to wag their tails and beg for pity, or to flatter with shoulders and smiles. Looking at the arrogance and imperiousness of the wealthy and powerful, they are often full of anger and unhappy. In fact, they are wrong! The way the wealthy and powerful look at us is not like the way we look at beggars and tramps, is it? Who of us is willing to treat beggars favorably or respect tramps? Of course, who among the wealthy and powerful will treat us favorably and respect us? In the current era, I am afraid that even if Zhuge Liang were reborn, there would definitely be no Liu Bei who would visit his thatched hut three times; let alone us! With this "understanding" of modern society, we will naturally be "calm" and "harmonious."

Ticket Office

Random Talk on Cartoons

— Qian Yun Writes, Wen Dongliang Draws

Shanghai's So-Called "Shoutou" (Fool)

"Shoutou" is originally something to celebrate, but in Shanghai, it is used to scold people!

For example, when you go to a Peking opera theater or cinema, you take a dollar to buy a ticket, and the ruthless person will find the change by using copper coins, dimes, and dime notes, tangling you up to the point of dizziness. Even when you finally finish calculating and hand it over, instead of praising you for being well-behaved, they scold you "Shoutou."

By analogy, those who can show off are understanding (well-behaved), while those who tighten their belts and hang themselves ("economical") are undoubtedly "Shoutou"!

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 21: Muttering Before the Lamp, Heartfelt Instructions to Weak Offspring; Strolling Under the Mountain, Coldly Watching Heroes

Gan Jizhi had been walking along, with his head down, lost in thought. He really hadn't expected that the person he was thinking about was walking towards him. At this moment, he heard someone say "Eh," and suddenly looked up, only to see Guizhi. Although he couldn't help but be startled, he was, after all, a person who often socialized outside, so he quickly calmed down, reached out and took off his hat, bowed to her with a smile and said, "Long time no see." Guizhi took two steps back, bit her lip, flicked her eyelids, smiled at him and said, "Gan-ye can say this to me, but I can't say this to Gan Er-ye." Jizhi said, "What are you talking about? I don't quite understand." Guizhi smiled and said, "A few days ago, I passed by your mansion's gate and saw Er-ye walking back and forth in the courtyard. Er-ye was busy and didn't see me." Jizhi held his hat in both hands and cupped his hands at her repeatedly, saying, "I'm so sorry!" Guizhi stayed where she was, two steps back, just staring at Jizhi with a smile on her face, without saying anything. Jizhi, because she had nothing to say, couldn't think of what to say in response for a moment. The two people stood facing each other in this desolate field, like a pair of stone figures. Jizhi immediately felt that this was not a solution, so he smiled at Guizhi and said, "Da Guniang, when will you give us wedding wine to drink? I'm glad to have made it back to Haidian this time in time for this opportunity." He was originally just making conversation, using this sentence to defuse the awkwardness of standing opposite each other. He didn't expect that if he hadn't said this, it would have been fine. As soon as he said this, Guizhi felt even more embarrassed; her cheeks were as if they were being baked by a stove, red all the way to the roots of her ears. The upper eyelids of her two eyes were drooping down at the same time, clustering out two lines of eyelashes. Two small fake jade leaf rings were hanging on her ears, and at this time, they suddenly fluttered and swayed, tumbling next to her neck, which showed how her muscles were trembling. (278)

Winter in the North

— Huang Kewei

The north country has neither intoxicating spring nor scorching summer. The four seasons are yellow sand flying and sunlight dim, showing a desolate and cold climate.

When the gentle and beautiful Jiangnan is the season of roaring north winds and thick frost covering tiles, the north country has become a world of ice and snow.

In the fields and valleys, it melts into a crystalline snow scene. The heavily laden camels, donkeys, and horses make crunching noises, leaving deep footprints. The fur merchants riding on high backs, wearing leather coats, with their ears and heads covered in furry leather hoods, but the hot air they exhale quickly condenses on their hard mustaches.

The rivers are frozen solid, even a strong hammer blow will only reveal a white line. So, the pleasure-seeking people are doing ice skating, or holding their partners, riding in snow sleds, sliding down the slopes, enjoying the snow scenery everywhere. How happy and peaceful they are!

But! In the world of ice and snow, we can no longer see the heroic anti-Japanese warriors, only the blood-red sun flag on the Great Wall, waving and flaunting its power in the north wind!

The broken rivers and mountains, the incomplete trenches, and the heroes' blood are all covered by white snow—the people whose blood has been chilled by the cold air have, of course, forgotten all the humiliating and tragic stories, and are infatuated with the beautiful snow scenery, and intoxicated by the masquerade ice skating party!

Talking from Experience

— Zikang

The time when a woman seems most lovable to us is when she has already said she doesn't love us anymore.

When you are so poor that you don't even have food to eat, you are especially easy to get hungry. It seems like you could eat four or five meals a day, but when you have food to eat, you often find it disgusting.

When you go back to your hometown, you feel that life in your hometown is very boring after only two days, but when you leave your hometown, you will think of the loveliness of your hometown.

Even if the rice you cook yourself is burnt and mushy, it always tastes better than the rice in the restaurant outside.

Short Story

Wax and Wane

— Tian Hensheng

After that, the days of returning became more and more distant from Ju Li, returning twice in three years, three and a half years, and six and a half years. After that, there was no news, not knowing where he was drifting. It was only rumored that Ah Quan's wife had died, and that he had remarried to a very young woman. But no one could know his exact situation. That he had more money now could be asserted with certainty, which could be inferred from the clothes and behavior of his three previous returns to his hometown, which were definitely not as poor as they had been fifteen years ago. In this way, everyone who knew Ah Quan, including his relatives, suddenly began to miss Ah Quan as if dying embers had rekindled. Everyone talked about Ah Quan with a sense of eager anticipation to see him; at the same time, they all instinctively thought that Ah Quan must have had a new story, and that he no longer wanted this hometown; from this speculation, it could also be known that Ah Quan would never return; the reason was that a major change had occurred in the Yu family, which everyone expected must have been known to Ah Quan, who did not want to send his daughter into a pit of poverty, which was why there had been no news for five or six years, and that there was no other reason than breaking off the engagement.

This news was indeed surprising. Fifteen years ago, Ah Quan was so poor that he only owned an old boat; now, the Yu family was so poor that they only owned three old houses, with nothing else of value. Mingfa had died of illness three years ago, and now there was only Mingfa's wife and son, Longsheng. Although Longsheng was already twenty-two years old, he was dull and unwilling to study when he was young, and later, because of poverty, he had to learn carpentry, earning very little money.

However, Longsheng felt the need to marry a wife very urgently. The fire of youth burned his entire soul, and the desire for the opposite sex filled his entire consciousness; when others remembered Ah Quan and talked about Ah Quan, he listened silently and imagined his fiancée, Xiaoling. In his imagination, Xiaoling was an extremely beautiful girl; although he had never really met her, in his dreams, he had met her many times, but he only vaguely remembered the face with which she had met him in his dreams.

Longsheng was eager to marry a wife, so he naturally asked his mother. His mother recalled the old story from fifteen years ago when Ah Quan wanted to marry her daughter to raise as a child bride. She regretted that she had not agreed at the time. If she had been a child bride, there would not be no news now, and perhaps she could have relied on Ah Quan's wealth to get some benefit. But regret was useless. For the sake of her son's request, she had to find a matchmaker. But at this time, Jiang Si-ye had also died. Zhu Changchun, who had originally been invited by Mingfa to be a helper matchmaker, did not take on this responsibility, and he also complained that her family had not agreed to the child bride in the first place. Every time she went to see Changchun, she returned home disappointed and powerless.

The extreme burning of the fire of youth caused Longsheng to lose his mind, and he actually thought that his mother was unwilling to find him a wife, and he often made a big fuss over it. The more he made a fuss, the more his mother regretted not agreeing to the child bride in the past, and the more saddened she was by the poverty now, and the more terrified she was of the future. If this continued, they would not become a family! Moreover, the speculation about Ah Quan's wealth gradually became confirmed. Someone met Ah Quan in a big city thousands of miles away, saying that he was much fatter than before and had a good complexion, and that he must have made a fortune. His mother was even more indescribably sad, but Longsheng hurriedly asked the person where he had met Ah Quan.

A few days later, Longsheng suddenly disappeared, his whereabouts unknown.

Foreign Exchange Still at 7%

Yesterday, the market trend was calmer than before. Because banks are still in the closed period and are not doing business due to holidays, only money shops and a few Chinese-owned banks were open for trading. Therefore, the inflow and outflow were unusually quiet. Various large-scale transactions were suspended, so it is not worth recording. The market price of foreign exchange is still 7%. As usual, there is no market price for transfers. Bank receipts and disbursements are also suspended. Various remittance funds over 400,000, customer source 100,000, disbursement 250,000, banknote recovery and issuance 1.3 million, foreign mortgage transactions over 500,000. It was said to be only 2 yuan and 5 fen, and one rumor said it was only 1 yuan and 9 jiao and 8 fen. In this case, it is naturally more difficult to boost people's hearts, and the future of Sanbu flour is feared to be even worse. As a result, this month fell by 2 fen and 7.5 li compared to the previous day, January fell by 3.5 fen, February fell by 3 fen, March fell by 2 fen and 7.5 li, April fell by 2 li and 5 li, and May fell by 3 fen.

83 Trucks of Wheat Delivered This Month

—Standard Wheat Market Extremely Quiet—

After the wheat market opened in the morning and afternoon, the market in each month showed a light and quiet state. Because foreign wheat has stopped trading and there is no quotation, there is little foreign meaning in the buying and selling of each month. Moreover, this month has passed, and there are fewer chips. Both long-term parties are watching, so the access is quiet again. As a result, only March was good for one point, and April was one point smaller. As for the standard delivery for this month, it has been fully fulfilled yesterday, with a total of 83 trucks, delivered by numbers 6, 19, 24, 27, and 35, and received by numbers 23 and 36.

The First Batch of Domestically Produced New Cotton Red Enters the Market in the Sugar Market

—Opening at 17 Yuan—

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was flat and tired. The association divided the market into 24 rough sand white ordinary divisions at 19 yuan and 6 jiao, with no rise or fall. The transshipment goods were 5 fen, which was 6 yuan and 7 jiao and a half. The 20th medium sand white high goods transshipped at 6 yuan and 7 jiao and a half, the 89th Dutch red transshipped at 7 yuan. Taikoo sugar was stable, still at 20 yuan and 6 jiao. Zhenji's own factory cotton white number one was 1 jiao smaller, at 18 yuan and 5 jiao and a half. Chao Gang number opened a new mention of green at 13 yuan and 7 jiao, also 1 jiao smaller, ordinary 12 yuan and 8 jiao also opened the first batch of new cotton red more than 100 bags, the price was 17 yuan.

Large Quantities of Quality Indigo Serge Selling Well

Yesterday, transactions in serge were mostly retail. Quality indigo serge, in particular, was selling briskly. Western tailoring shops and fashionable women's clothing stores are continually purchasing it, mostly for making men's and women's leather overcoats, hence the current strong sales of both Chinese and foreign indigo serge. Fabrics priced around seven yuan are selling especially well. Both local and national capital traders are importing large quantities, and its rapid turnover is currently unmatched by any other woolen fabric. Domestically produced "Zhanghua" brand indigo serge sells for seven and a half yuan, Japanese indigo serge for seven yuan, "Shenchuan Tuo" indigo serge for seven and a half yuan, and "Lihe" for thirteen yuan four jiao.

Free Talk

From Changing to Deepening

— Ruoye

Many books on the cultivation of writers often mention the issue of "changing environments."

The meaning of "changing environments," as Shiramura Togyu [TN: Cook River White Village, a Japanese author] said, is to discover "a new self." To put it more plainly, it means that writers should constantly change their living environments, using continuous new life experiences to enrich themselves and their works. Only in this way can the wellspring of creativity not dry up, and the life of creation remain eternally fresh.

Recently, I saw a conversation by Hollywood star and writer Elizabeth Landi. Her main point was, "You can't maintain your youth even if you live in a beauty salon. Your spirit, your thoughts, your entire life plan must have a vibrant spring atmosphere, and then your face can reflect your youth." This is of course talking about how women should maintain their youth. In it, she also explains that "the greatest enemy of human age is monotony in life," and she advocates that life should be constantly "changed," starting with the arrangement of indoor furniture. The meaning is also to advise people to "change environments" to increase the interest in life and to maintain an eternally fresh spirit. This extends the issue of "changing environments" beyond writers to all aspects of life.

Is it really true that simply being able to constantly "change environments" can enrich one's life and keep one's life fresh? I think this is not entirely reliable. Naturally, "changing life" can help writers enrich and refresh the content of their works, and ordinary people can increase their interest in life. However, this does not prove that they have deepened their understanding of life, and that they are developing themselves through a deepened understanding of life. I believe that what is more important is not "changing environments" to obtain a constant surprise in life, but being able to deeply "understand life." To put it together, deepening one's understanding of life is of primary importance, and "changing life" is relatively secondary. If you don't understand life, what is the point of "changing environments" every day?

Do you want to enrich your life and your works? If possible, you can often "change environments," but you must first deepen your own understanding of life, I add in this way.

New Feelings About Old Things

— Xu Maoyong

The world's largest Bible, and the fourth-century Codex Sinaiticus, is indeed a precious antiquity. But Russia, which had such an antiquity, did not know how to cherish it, and instead gave it to the British Museum, and used the price of 100,000 pounds to buy machinery from England.

This will make people think of the XXXXX and Mr. X's corruption case in our country, and what I think of is another matter that is also somewhat related to Mr. X.

A few years ago, China had a school that required students to study and work at the same time. I was once a student there. One year, our class was assigned to practice in a metalworking shop. However, for a long time, we could not get work. At that time, the world economic panic had not yet occurred, and our factory was not related to the market at all, and would not be affected by foreign influences. The reason why we had no work was simply because the school could not receive funding and could not afford raw materials. However, it is really ridiculous to say that, for example, in the metalworking shop, we did not really work, but just played around, so we did not need a lot of iron as raw material. According to estimates, the school authorities only needed to spend fifty yuan per month to cover our consumption. However, it is said that they really could not even come up with fifty yuan.

But once, we discovered a strange thing. In the workshop, there were actually many workers smashing large machines one by one. A truck was waiting outside the workshop to transport the goods. We asked the workers and learned that it was the idea of the workshop director to sell these machines to another factory as scrap iron. This made us very angry. Selling good machines as scrap iron, having so much scrap iron to sell without distributing a little to us as raw material, and we also knew that this was the director's personal idea, without the approval of the school affairs meeting. Based on these three points, we determined that the director had committed a major crime, so we issued declarations, sent telegrams, and accused the director to all the faculty, staff, and students of the school and to the president in Nanjing.

The president was also furious when he heard the news, so he specially sent a committee to the school to investigate. The investigation meeting was held in the president's office. In addition to the committee members, the secretary-general, representatives of the faculty and staff, representatives of the student union, our representatives as plaintiffs, the accused director, and an industrial expert were also present. In the two-hour debate, the defendant finally ran out of arguments, and the various cover-up methods he had set up were also broken one by one by the plaintiffs. When the truth was about to be revealed, the industrial expert suddenly stood up and said that the workshop director was indeed lacking in procedures, but there was no crime of destroying machines. As an expert, he dared to conclude that those machines were really useless and equivalent to scrap iron.

This case ended like this. Both the plaintiff and the defendant were innocent. Because from the committee members to us, none of us were industrial experts, and we could not refute the expert's words, even though we clearly saw these machines were still able to produce two months ago.

From then on, I finally understood the organization of the behind-the-scenes and the wonderful use of experts, and I also understood a kind of great sophistication by analogy.

Smashing good machines and selling them as scrap iron is different from exchanging useless X things for expensive machines. This is the difference between a declining old family and a newly rich household, and also the difference between China and Russia today.

Geography Class

— Li Huiying

The teacher stood on the platform, opened a map of the Republic of China made in the twenty-first year of the Republic (1932), hung it next to the blackboard, and pointed out the borders of "Manchukuo" to the students. As the pointer moved on the map, he explained:

"Look, from here, to here, then a turn, to here, to here, then back to here, this is the border of 'Manchukuo'."

He started from Shanhaiguan, pointing along the coast, then to the Yalu River, the Tumen River, then up to the Ussuri River, the Heilong River, down to the Ergun River, the border of Mongolia, Chahar all the way to the Great Wall, and back to the original position of Shanhaiguan.

"Have you seen it clearly? Do you understand? This is the border of 'Manchukuo'."

He asked the thirty-odd elementary school students below the stage, unexpectedly, more than half of the small hands in the seats were raised. According to the seating arrangement, he was going to ask the students about their doubts.

"Hu Nanshan, what don't you understand?"

Hu Nanshan sat in the first row and stood up, saying in a grand manner:

"Teacher, this is a map of the Republic of China, how come there is a 'Manchukuo'?"

He did not answer immediately, intending to ask all the students who raised their hands, and then answer together. He told Hu Nanshan to sit down and asked other students.

"Didn't the teacher say last year that the three northeastern provinces are Chinese territory?"

"Teacher, does Jehol also belong to 'Manchukuo'? Wasn't it also part of China before?"

"If 'Manchukuo' is not China, then we are not Chinese either!"

After asking all the students who raised their hands, they all asked the same kind of questions.

He was stumped.

Logically, he also knew about this matter; how "Manchukuo" was established, how "Manchukuo" came to possess Chinese land, and who created "Manchukuo". However, he couldn't say it directly. If he did, he would not want his life anymore - the Japanese would definitely arrest him and behead him.

But this aroused his infinite sadness, for himself, for these elementary school students, he felt that there were more people who were slaves to the Japanese Empire under the name of "Manchukuo" and could never turn over.

He stood blankly on the platform, and two huge hot tears unexpectedly welled up in his eyes.

"'Manchukuo' - is - newly established, - is - separated from - China."

After a while, he could only say this stutteringly, perfunctorily answering the students' questions. He thought that after saying this, he would bear the pain and rush through the lesson, but this still did not satisfy the students' desire for answers. In their young minds, they immediately recalled the traces of the riots in cities and villages after the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident). They also knew somewhat that the Japanese created "Manchukuo" and separated a large piece of land from the Chinese map, so they changed the topic and asked:

"Teacher, how was 'Manchukuo' established?"

"Teacher, teacher, who separated 'Manchukuo' from China?"

He wanted to get rid of the students' encirclement, but not only was it impossible, but the students became even more eager to pester him. Now the questions asked by the students were even more serious and practical. Because of his own difficult situation, he suddenly thought of Daudet's "The Last Lesson". Compared to that, he and the students below the stage were even more unfortunate than the characters in that novel. That old teacher could still inject a final stimulant into the students, but he didn't dare to say even half a word about the bad things about the Japanese.

What to do? If a teacher cannot satisfy the students' desires, then the students will despise him, especially some elementary school students, who use the teacher's ability to answer questions as a condition for judging whether the teacher is good or bad.

"'Manchukuo' was created by Japanese imperialism - " He was about to answer the students truthfully, regardless of everything, but coincidentally, the bell rang to end the class, which was undoubtedly a benefactor who rescued him from his predicament. He hurriedly packed up the map, not even having the courage to glance at the students below the stage, and casually said, "Class dismissed, let's talk about it next time," and hurriedly left the classroom.

Two Brothers (71)

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

"Let me speak… Listen… I have many things to say to you, to make you understand… But you won't understand… Because… if you want me to stay… then it must be… no, I can't…"

"Speak, Mother, speak."

"Alright! I'll speak. At least I didn't deceive you… You want me to stay with you, don't you? For this reason, so that we can still see each other, still talk, still bump into each other in the same room all day long—because I'm afraid to open the door now, fearing that I'll see your brother behind that door—for this reason, don't forgive me—nothing is more unbearable than forgiveness—but don't feel angry at all about what I did before… You need to feel very strong, feel different from others, so that you can think that you are not Roland's son without blushing, without despising me… I've suffered enough… I've suffered too much, I can't suffer anymore, no, I can't suffer anymore! And my suffering didn't start yesterday, it's been a long time… But you won't understand this, you! So that we can still live together, still hug each other, my little Zhe'an, you can well imagine that although I was your father's mistress, I was actually more like his wife, his true wife. I feel no shame at all about this. I regret nothing. He's dead now and I still love him. I will always love him. I've only loved him. He was my whole life, all my happiness, all my hope, all my comfort, my everything. For such a long time, he was my everything! Listen to me, my little darling, I can say before God that if I hadn't met him, there would be no interest in my life, nothing, no affection, no tenderness, none of that which makes us feel very regretful about the time we grow old, nothing! Everything I have was given to me by him! In this world, I only had him, followed by you two, your brother and you. Without you, my life would be empty, as dark and empty as night. If I hadn't met him, then I wouldn't have loved anything, wouldn't have known anything, wouldn't have hoped for anything, wouldn't even have cried.—Because I have cried, my little Zhe'an. Ah! Yes, I have cried, ever since we came here. I gave him my whole self, body and soul, permanently, happily, and I can declare before the God who paired us together that for more than ten years, I was his wife just as he was my husband. Later, I knew that he didn't love me as passionately as before. He was always kind and attentive, but I wasn't the same in his eyes as before. That was the end! Ah! How I cried!… Life is so base and cunning!… Nothing lasts… So we moved here; and I never saw him again. He never came… He always said in his letters that he would come… I kept waiting for him!… And I never saw him again… And now he's dead… But since he thought of you, then he must still love us. As for me, I will still love him when I take my last breath. I will never deny that I love him, and I love you because you are his son. I can't feel ashamed in front of you because of him! Do you understand? I can't! If you want me to stay, then you must agree to be his son, and we must talk about him from time to time. You must love him a little, and we must think of him when we look at each other. If you don't want to, if you can't, then goodbye forever, my little darling. We can't stay together now! Whatever you want me to do, I will do."

Zhe'an replied in a gentle voice:

"Stay, Mother."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Official Addiction and Official Famine

— Lizhai

This year, the civil service examinations held separately in Beijing and Ping (Peiping, present-day Beijing) officially recruited more than eight hundred people, and those who failed were around two thousand. This phenomenon not only illustrates the difficulty of finding an outlet for Chinese intellectuals, but also shows that the number of Chinese citizens who want to be officials is still higher than that of any other profession.

Secondly, whenever the North China Political Affairs Readjustment Council is established, or the Hubei, Jiangsu, or a certain provincial government is reorganized, those newly appointed dignitaries invariably post notices to fend off requests, saying "willing to recruit, but unable to place" (meaning they have too many recommendations and not enough positions). But in fact, each new dignitary receives thousands of letters of recommendation, at least eight hundred. Also, the hotels in the central and provincial capitals and commercial ports, whenever a ministry or provincial government is reorganized, are usually fully booked. Nine out of ten of these travelers with a bag and a belly full of hope come from afar to "look for work" (a "modern" way of saying "to become an official"). All these facts, on the one hand, reflect the depth of people's "official addiction," which is still "unshakeable" despite "revolution," and on the other hand, show that in this era, there are more people seeking "officialdom" than before, resulting in an "official famine" due to oversupply. The seriousness of the "official famine" problem for the national economy and the people's livelihood is no less than that of rural bankruptcy!

Why is "official addiction" more deeply ingrained in people than "ideological belief," something they never forget? Because: from the perspective of those who want to be "officials," they have clearly been inspired by the fact that nine out of ten of the "officials" who were previously appointed to positions have made a fortune, and they understand that the gains from being an "official" are actually greater than those from any other occupation, whether scholar, farmer, worker, or merchant. Secondly, from the perspective of the general public towards those who are "officials," they are still mostly admired and envied, just like Su Ji's sister-in-law's view - "because my husband's position is high and he has a lot of money"?

Why has the phenomenon of "official famine" become so widespread and serious? Because: first, everyone wants to be an official, so naturally there are too many monks and not enough porridge, resulting in the phenomenon of monks scrambling around because they can't get rice. Second, the common practice of government in China is not to find people because of the job, but to assign jobs because of the people. The occupation of administrative "officials" has no guarantee, and their fate depends on the arrival and departure of political "officials." Since the rise and fall of the boss is "full of illusions in the official career," the assistants naturally have the panic of "packing up and leaving" at any time.

The result of the "official famine" deepening day by day is naturally "disaster officials" all over China!

Where do "disaster officials" go? This depends on the rank of the "disaster official." Small "disaster officials" do not suffer so much because their "official status" or "official face" is not very important, so they may as well change their profession and re-enter the ranks of scholars, farmers, workers, and merchants, or even pull rickshaws. However, there are also those who have no other skills besides being "officials" or whose "official addiction" is too deep and who cannot point the way out when hungry. Therefore, we often see news of "disaster officials" "dying for their cause." The most serious problem is the "big disaster officials" above the rank of senior official. Most of them are "anxious and uneasy without an official for three days"! However, it is easy to step down, but it is most difficult to step up. They have no choice but to find a way out when there is no way out. As a result, these "big disaster officials" become politicians who "fear that the world will not be in chaos." The first question these people think about in their hearts and say in their mouths is "will there be changes in the political situation"? Because only with "change" can new people who play with guns and cannons come out to "obey heaven and respond to the people," which will inevitably break the rice bowls of a group of current "officials" and turn them into "disaster officials." And these "old disaster officials" who hope for "change" have endless opportunities to escape "disaster," get rid of their predicament, and jump onto the stage.

Afterwards, like a revolving lantern, it is the turn of the newly dismissed "disaster officials" (most of whom are full and not really "disaster," but still do not want to be neglected) to hope for "changes in the political situation" or create "changes in the political situation."

"If poor, then change." Changes follow changes, and the "Great China Stage" that bears the brunt of these "changes" is unimaginable!

Page 18

Talking about the National Products Year

— Xiaosheng

Last year, I was a minor assistant in a XXX National Products Promotion Association, burying my head in writing all day long. What I wrote was always nothing more than saying that foreign goods are imported by several hundred million yuan every year, and our country is now at a critical juncture of life and death. If the people of the country do not wake up again, the country will soon perish. The following is to promote how good the current national products are, and how they are better than imported goods. However, for our panicked national psyche, using the idea of national demise or not as a strong stimulant is not the best approach. Anyway, they believe that Shanghai, which has been under the rule of foreign powers for decades, is a place where people live and work in peace and contentment, and has never experienced a panic. Only the miserable friends in the mainland flee back and forth when they encounter natural disasters and man-made calamities. Although the news of the January 28th Incident was reported in the newspapers as something shocking, in fact, those living in the concessions were still at peace. Although dozens of planes were buzzing overhead, as if watching the movie "The Aviation World," the unlucky ones were only the Zhabei area in the Chinese part of the city, which became a scorched earth. Therefore, it is better to be ruthless and turn the whole country into concessions like Shanghai. Wouldn't that be a world of favorable weather and prosperity? Therefore, many compatriots, hearing the propaganda of national products and the country's demise, instead wanted to bring up their great feelings of lifting a stone and pressing their own feet.

I remember that just today last year, I was concentrating on writing big advertisements for the National Products Year, preparing for the National Products Year motorcade parade on New Year's Day, fully expecting that with the sound of firecrackers bidding farewell to the old and welcoming the new, under the tune of universal renewal, national products would eventually spread like wildfire and sell well throughout the country. Under the national spirit of my Chinese descendants, foreign goods would naturally disappear. Although this was just my wishful thinking, everyone believed that this year's imports of foreign goods would be at least discounted compared to previous years. However, the National Products Year has passed from the beginning to the end of the year. According to the figures reported by the International Trade Bureau to the government, the trade deficit was written unceremoniously as more than 474 million yuan, and it is estimated that the figure of 900 million yuan will be reached by the end of the year, which is the highest record of trade deficit in previous years. It is simply an unprecedented trade deficit phenomenon since the opening of trade. It is unknown whether this is enough to show the people's material progress and the so-called "Chinese people are rich in commercial ethics" by a certain important British figure?

I heard that next year, the Republic of China's 23rd year (1934), will be changed to the Women's National Products Year. Today's newspapers already have several groups coming forward to initiate it, and they are busy applying to the government for registration. They will also hold a large-scale motorcade parade on New Year's Day next year. Talking about the results of this year's National Products Year is like pouring a basin of cold water. Probably in the eyes of the gentlemen who are persevering and enthusiastic in promoting national products, they think that this year's unexpected and chilling results are all due to the women's lack of help. Therefore, as long as women use less powder and wear less imported silk, they will definitely succeed. But what exactly? Nothing has started yet, so there is no result to talk about. I have not studied fortune-telling, let alone predict, so I have to wait until later.

But I must say this: Is the demise or survival of a country entirely determined by whether the people use national products or not? This is indeed a problem. But because of the length of the intention, it can only be put aside for now. Now, let's take a hundred or a thousand steps back: If our country's market can cut off foreign goods, then I think even the ladies, mistresses, and officials who have always liked to buy foreign goods, would not die on empty foreign goods boxes, would they? On the other hand, the farmers work hard to cultivate the land for a year, and after paying all the taxes and land taxes, what is left is not enough for the cost of land fertilizer. The workers work hard all day and are not enough to feed themselves. Under this whip of life, they will naturally choose the cheaper ones for daily necessities. Where do they have the gentlemanly care to distinguish whether this is a national product or that is a foreign product? This is a matter of human nature, the same mind, the same reason.

The Women's National Products Year is about to begin, and our hope, of course, is that we can get a good result. But if it still happens to be on par with this year (this is just in case, not schadenfreude, I hereby declare), then in the 24th year of the National Products Year, I will be the first to advocate that it should be changed to the "Military National Products Year." The endless civil wars that have occurred over the years have done millions upon millions of business with foreign countries. If the warlord masters of the whole country can change to using national products because of the National Products Year, and further because there are no national products, everyone does not use them, then at that time, it will not be impossible to prevent foreign goods from entering our country's market, and national products can be promoted without having to be advocated.

Although this is a pile of nonsense, I think it is at least the wish of hundreds of millions of ordinary people!

One Time, Another Time

— Where to Go

When a person is sick, they always think this way: What if I get well right away? Then I can do things that I can't do, I can do things that are difficult to do, and I can even do things that I don't like to do. But once a person gets better, although the words are still remembered, and the ability to do things is still the same, the heart has changed in every way. I always feel that this is "one time, another time." The previous words seem to be said only in the previous environment.

The same is true for the generally frustrated people. They always think that one day they will be successful, their temperament will be more generous, money will often be lent, they will always be more polite to others, and cars will never run over poor people on the road. When they are really successful, things are quite different. Generosity has turned into stinginess, money is tightly held in the purse, and the attitude towards others is cold, as if wanting to eat them. The words said before, even if remembered, will be explained with various reasons. What generosity is foolish, saving is necessary, being polite to others is not allowed, driving a car slowly will delay things and waste fuel, etc., the words are like flowing water, said without a bit of thought.

What kind of argument is this? Think about it, it seems very mysterious. In fact, if you think about it carefully, it is just two sides of human nature. One side is prepared for fantasy, and the other side is prepared for reality. Because it is always rare for a person to want to be successful and be successful. If one is not successful, one cannot help but fantasize, and once one fantasizes, it seems that one will not be blessed by the gods if one does not become a good person; it is as if entering a temple and making a vow will not get the blessing of the gods. When one is successful, one can naturally ignore these things. As long as one ascends to the throne, the previous words, even if recognized as nonsense, recognized as bullshit, are up to him!

The Editor of the Supplement

— Wang Ci

"Of all the strange flavors in the world, none is worse than the suffering of the supplement editor!"

This sentence is neither "said by the ancients" nor "XX maxim": it is experience that tells me to fabricate it.

So, what is the suffering exactly? Well, let me tell you!

Too many manuscripts are submitted, but the space of the supplement is only so large. Looking at the submissions, they are all "masterpieces" crafted with painstaking effort. If I publish this one, I inevitably have to give up that one; therefore, I hesitate and feel the suffering in my heart; this is the first suffering!

Too few manuscripts are submitted. I piece them together from here and there, but it is still not enough. I flip through the old manuscripts, but they have all lost their timeliness. I have to fill in the blanks myself, so I borrow the power of cigarettes in the hope of "composing a poem in seven steps" and "writing thousands of words at a stroke"; unexpectedly, desire and reality often become the opposite: the more I force myself, the slower it becomes! I stare at the manuscript paper, feeling at a loss and achieving nothing! I feel the suffering in my heart; this is the second suffering!

Manuscripts are sent by relatives and friends, and there are often those that have no value for publication; however, he is my brother-in-law! He is my classmate! He is my acquaintance! He is my student! If I publish them, I am afraid of losing my "newspaper style"; if I abandon them, I am afraid of losing my "friendship". I think back and forth, and there is no suitable solution! I feel the suffering in my heart; this is the third suffering!

There are some contributors who have a very large output; they even send a manuscript every day, but there are very few good ones. Although I don't publish them, I can't frustrate their perseverance in submitting manuscripts. Their works are indeed not good, but their spirit is truly commendable! In the end, I abandon them without publishing them, and my heart is always uneasy; this is the fourth suffering!

If I am not careful in selecting manuscripts, I can easily be caught by critics who are good at "nitpicking," and scolded. Although I endure and swallow my anger, and imitate Ah Q's spiritual victory method, I am still somewhat disappointed; this is the fifth suffering!

Or a few sentences are added to the manuscript, saying that my family cannot afford to pay for school, and I rely entirely on the fees from this submission to maintain my studies, or saying that there is an economic panic, and please publish more to maintain my livelihood. How can such a pitiful attitude not move people's hearts? This is the sixth suffering!

Or when writing filler material, I am too arbitrary, and unintentionally offend the authorities, resulting in reprimands, warnings, and... Therefore, I always have a warning in my heart when I write, and my heart is uneasy; this is the seventh suffering!

The suffering of supplement editors is numerous! How can there be only "seven sufferings"!

Back Room Drama

— Lingling

Another sleepless night to curse; the clock has already struck two. I'm still tossing and turning on a makeshift wooden bed in a cramped back room, unable to sleep. I don't know if it's because the weather has gotten colder lately and the comforter is too thin, or if the neurasthenia I've been free of for over a year has relapsed. I'm truly worried about myself. I've tried repeatedly to calm down and banish all thoughts, but the more I try to calm down, the more flustered I become, and the less I can sleep.

After some time, the back door downstairs creaked open, followed by the sounds of conversation, footsteps on the stairs, and coughs, shattering the quiet and cold of the late night. I knew it was my landlord and his wife returning. The front room door opened, then the lights were switched on, the wardrobe opened, conversations and whispers were exchanged, the thermos was opened, water was poured, and there was the soft, emotional laughter of a woman... Suddenly, the air became much livelier. But this sudden change in the atmosphere made my mind feel hazy, and I had a floating sensation.

"You son of a bitch, you dare play around again; give it back, you dare not give it back!" Before I had even fallen asleep, a sharp, fierce scream came from the front room through the cracks in the wall, waking me from the hazy dreamland I had just entered. I was shocked, stretched my head out further, and strained my ears to listen.

"Tell me! Who did you steal it to give to? You black-hearted bastard, you son of a bitch! Give it back, give it back!" It was still the woman's voice, with a crying and scolding tone.

The man didn't respond; the woman started sobbing, muttering through gritted teeth, "You son of a bitch, you black-hearted devil."

Perhaps the woman's scolding was too intense, enraging the man: "Damn it!" A thunderous roar shook the thin walls, "So what? I took it, I gave it to the one I love, what are you going to do about it? Scold? You scold again, and I'll beat you!"

"You son of a bitch, you black-hearted devil! Stealing my things to please some rotten whore, not admitting your mistake, and you still want to hit me? Hmph, go ahead and hit me, I dare you to hit me." The woman didn't soften in the face of the threat.

"I'll hit you, I'll just hit you!" *Slap, slap*, the sound of a palm connecting with a fleshy face, crisp and loud. She was rolling on the floor, her heels drumming against the floorboards, screaming shrilly, mixed with the sound of phlegm and snot; she wasn't begging for mercy, but she wasn't as tough as before either: "Okay, hit me, I'll let you beat me to death, if you don't beat me to death tonight, you're not a man! Beat me to death, so you, you son of a bitch, can bring that slut and rotten whore into the house to have fun... Hit me, hit me hard... Hit me,... Help, murder!..."

The man silently and mercilessly rained blows on the body rolling on the floor, the woman continued to cry out loudly: at first, she mixed it with harsh scolding, but later she cried more and more mournfully, "Help! Murder!"

This continued for another ten minutes or so. By this time, the sister-in-law in the attic room, Mr. and Mrs. Wang in the front parlor downstairs, Mr. Zhang in the back parlor, and the maid, Little Sheng, and her old, trembling-lipped nanny in the kitchen, I don't believe that these tenants could still be comfortably seeking their own sweet dreams in their beds: logically, I also don't believe that the tragic cries for "help" wouldn't strike their hearts and have some impact. However, despite the shouting, every room remained silent; although I had only moved in a week ago, I was used to this kind of thing, and I knew there was definitely no danger to life, so I felt annoyed, buried my head in the comforter, and plugged my ears with my fingers.

But the commotion in the front room intensified, tables, chairs, and the bed were moved from their original positions, teacups and washbasins rolled on the floor with their mistress, something struck the window, and shards of glass fell into the courtyard... the man shouted "Hit!" the woman cried "Help!"...

Suddenly, the man dragged the woman out into the corridor, the sound of blows raining down right next to my bed; things had probably gotten serious, and it seemed that only a third party could intervene to stop it. The sister-in-law in the attic room, under this urgent need, stepped forward righteously, but she only stood at her doorway, saying:

"You're husband and wife, you were fine during the day, what's so important that you have to fight in the middle of the night, it's really not worth it, is it?"

There was no response, the beating continued; so she walked up, dragging the woman back into the room as she said:

"Oh dear, what a sin, in this cold weather, wearing only a thin shirt and sleeping on the ground, what if you get frostbite? Husband and wife should talk things over, why make such a fuss... Mr. Lin, give her a break, look, you've already swollen her head... Mrs. Lin, rest, we can talk about it tomorrow."

"Sister-in-law in the attic room, you don't understand, this shrew is really a cheapskate, you can't give in to her, I wouldn't be satisfied even if I beat her to death tonight." The man's words were obviously rushed.

But the woman, seeing that someone had come and was defending her and blaming the man, no longer just cried out for help, she said in a sobbing voice: "Okay, hit me again, sister-in-law in the Hengzi room, he stole my bracelet to give to a whore, and he's still acting violently! Okay, watch this short-lived ghost beat me to death... I've suffered enough, I'm willing to be beaten to death by you... Hit me... If you don't beat me to death tonight, you're not a good man!"

The man didn't answer, seeming to move to hit her again, but the sister-in-law in the Hengzi room held him back, "Mr. Lin, listen to me, don't fight at night, whatever it is, we'll talk about it tomorrow, we can only do so much as cohabitants, if you keep fighting, and someone dies, there's nothing we can do."

The man stopped, and the woman obediently stopped crying. The sister-in-law in the Hengzi room triumphantly walked back to her Hengzi room. Here, in the front room, the man seemed to go to bed first, and the woman was still sitting at the table, sobbing. Soon, the sound of the light switch being turned off could be heard.

The air was unexpectedly quiet again, but this silence after the great commotion was a major threat to me! I more calmly covered my head with the thin comforter, but my mind was unusually clear because my body felt numbly cold, and my heart was even more flustered and nervous. No matter what, I couldn't allow myself to enter that floating state again.

But the tired man and woman in the front room were responding, sometimes with a mixture of snores, loudly transmitting from the cracks in the wall to the back room.

Disaster!

People! People!

Amateur Mailbox

Not Allowed to Overstep

Editor Sir:

I have a friend who works as a laborer at a film company; last August, he returned to his hometown to get married. This marriage was arranged by his parents, with a matchmaker's word, and it has been a year and a half. Because one was in the hometown and one was in Shanghai, there were many inconveniences, so he brought his wife to Shanghai. Coincidentally, I have a three-story apartment, which I couldn't refuse to lend to them. Unexpectedly, the two of them fight and quarrel every day. It's also unbearable that I can't sleep. Also, his wife is very vain. One night, I accidentally heard his wife scolding, "Others are wearing Western suits, and I married you, a poor wretch who doesn't even have a Western suit." My friend replied, "After I die, you can marry a friend who wears Western suits, as you please, but while I'm alive here, I won't allow it." Poor friend of mine, after saying these few words, she bit his thigh until it was covered in blood, and he couldn't even run away. He's a laborer, and he needs to move around all day. How can he endure this situation for long? There's really no way. Please advise me on three things:

(1) Should he divorce her in the shortest possible time? Or what?

(2) My friend is a laborer, illiterate, and naturally unqualified to wear a Western suit. What should he do?

(3) Second landlords in Shanghai have the right to freedom. If I don't allow them to live there, will it harm my friendship with my friend? I hope for a response in your esteemed publication, and I would be extremely grateful. Respectfully,

Zhang Gaoshou

Editor's Note: Mr. Zhang's first question cannot be established, even if it comes from his friend voluntarily; a minor injury caused by marital discord cannot be a condition for divorce. If your friend has no motivation for divorce himself, then Mr. Zhang absolutely cannot overstep or satirically implement it. Under this system of transactional marriage, it is not easy for a laborer to marry a wife. If you advise him to divorce, he will most likely regret it. To deal with this unreasonable wife, you can only use some husband's rights, as long as you don't intend to abuse her. When she lays hands on you, it wouldn't be wrong to give her a few back. In today's Chinese middle and lower classes, this method is very common; and the results are not bad. Marital love is not severed because of it. In the event that your friend is truly weak and incompetent, you, as bystanders, can only go as far as providing support and intimidation, and cannot go any further.

The second question, then of course there is no reason to cater to her.

The third question, endure as much as you can to preserve friendship; when it becomes unbearable, you can only state your difficulties and ask him to move out. Your friend will naturally realize his mistake and will not complain to you.

Novel

Shanghai (28)

— Zhang Laosan

(Forty-One) Let's Hope So

Little Huang was especially excited today, rushing in and out all day, too busy to cope. He would grab someone and talk for only a few words, as if there was some important event, and then talk to someone else, but what he said was all irrelevant. Suddenly, he thought of going for a walk, and without my agreement, he forced me to run outside. The cold wind outside was blowing hard, and the small trees on the roadside were swaying as if they couldn't bear the pressure and were about to droop. There were so few people on Avenue Joffre, and even those who passed by had their heads buried in their coat collars, hurrying along. The usually straight-lined foreign girls and the foreign gentlemen in stylish Western suits were no longer leisurely strolling on the sidewalks, and the White Russian descendants who catered to the sailors were no longer flashing their seductive eyes. Trams passed by, followed by cars, and the sound seemed even more desolate now. We lowered our heads, counting our steps as we slowly walked, not saying a word, looking like two homeless wanderers.

In the display windows on both sides of the road, the Christmas decorations had lost their effect under the bright lights. Santa Claus, carrying all kinds of gifts, stood alone in the cotton-made snow scene, so lonely. He was unable to grab the attention of passers-by, and after a few days of sorrow, he would be replaced by other beautiful decorations. The time to welcome him once a year was so lively, but after only a few days, he had been abandoned by the people who had welcomed him.

I reached into my pocket and fiddled with a few copper coins, not even understanding why I was idly pondering these facts. I casually pulled out a pack of cigarettes, offered one to Little Huang, and we both stopped at the same time, our heads huddled together, trying to resist the invasion of the cold wind and light a fire.

"Mister" an accented English voice and a dark shadow blocked our path.

I looked up and saw a descendant of a White Russian aristocratic family, wearing a worn Western suit, no coat, no tie, shrugging his shoulders, raising his hand towards us, looking poor and pleading.

"Sorry" I patted my pocket, I pulled out a cigarette and gave it to him "Smoking?"

"Thank You"! He took the cigarette, quickly took out a lighter and lit it, so naturally, letting me inhale the smoke. He retreated to the front of a Russian restaurant, raising his shoulders even higher, almost obscuring his head.

We continued to walk forward, seeing a cloud of thick smoke coming out of his invisible collar, one after another, continuously.

"Pitiable"! I said.

"When we get to that point, I wonder if there will be a gentleman patting his pocket to donate a cigarette?"

"Little Huang, you seem to have lost your senses today."

"Really. Our lives are too insecure. These days, the situation in Shanghai is full of rumors. One day, when the imperialist artillery invades Zhabei, we..." He stopped, seeming unable to find the appropriate words.

"Since the Wan case," I said, "the imperial ambitions have been completely exposed, and the Shenyang Night incident was even more arrogant of the royal military, but... Shanghai, I think, won't go that far..."

"Let's hope so."
