Film Special

The Glitter of Hollywood

— Fu

Unfortunately, all hidden in the vault and cannot be taken out

Experts estimate the total value at around twenty million

Everyone knows the extravagance and wastefulness of Hollywood stars, so in their pursuit of luxury and pleasure, they naturally cannot be without shiny things to adorn various parts of their bodies. The most valuable of these shiny things is of course diamonds, followed by various gems and pearls. Silver and gold are countless. But do you know how many diamonds and jewels these Hollywood stars have? According to an estimate by a large jeweler in Los Angeles, Hollywood's investment in jewelry totals as much as US$15 million. Another Hollywood jeweler said that all the jewelry in Hollywood, when added up, is worth about US$20 million. These two jewelers are major suppliers of jewelry to Hollywood. Their business investigations are of course very reliable.

But it's very sad that even with perfect pearl necklaces, large diamond bracelets, rings, etc., they cannot be worn, but must be locked in large steel vaults in large banks. When they have time, they run to the bank, open their own jewelry box, play with it for a while, then carefully put it back, lock it, and come out empty-handed. This is like loving children, raising them in the hospital, rarely seeing them, and being reluctant to part with them. But Hollywood, which is full of jewelry, is ultimately inappropriate, and many people have been robbed before. The most famous times were the misfortunes of Zeppo Marx, Mae West, Maureen O'Sullivan, and Bette Davis. Therefore, they are all afraid to show their real jewelry to the public.

The only exception is Lupe Velez. She is the protagonist of "Pagan Paradise," a famous Mexican cat, a bold and sassy woman. She is not afraid of robbers. She even carries a handgun on her body, ready to resist robbers. She also has a bodyguard, who is Johnny Weissmuller, the Tarzan in "Tarzan the Ape Man," who is also her lover. Their marriage has been rumored for a long time.

When it comes to the richest collection among Hollywood stars, everyone says it is Marion Davies. Experts estimate that it is between US$250,000 and US$500,000. In this year of economic depression, everyone is poor, but Marion Davies is still able to take out money to buy jewelry. Recently, she bought an emerald bracelet and a similar brooch from a New York jeweler, for a total price of around US$40,000. Although Marion Davies' collection is so rich, she doesn't dare to wear it herself, except at very small private gatherings. She used to be very casual, often wearing a large gem on a silver fox coat and hanging it in the dressing room of a large theater. Once, while she was filming a movie, she casually stuffed a large brooch on her chest into a reporter's pocket and then forgot about it. Later, when the reporter returned home, his wife searched his pocket and found the gem-diamond-encrusted brooch, and had a big fight with him. Later, he fortunately remembered Marion Davies and rushed to return it to her. Marion was still indifferent, but in fact, the brooch was worth US$15,000.

Another romantic star, Peggy Hopkins Joyce, may have a collection even larger than Marion Davies'. But she herself says that she doesn't dare to bring her things to Hollywood. Most of her collection is stored in bank vaults in Chicago. Some are stored in Paris. The most famous Joyce diamond was originally owned by an Indian prince, weighing one hundred and fifty carats and worth more than US$500,000. There is also a string of pearls that she bought in Europe, but she stores it in Paris. It is said that because the import tax on the string of pearls would be US$80,000, she said she couldn't afford it! Joyce has been divorced many times. These many things were all bought for her by several ex-husbands, but it is too sad that she doesn't dare to wear them. She also doesn't want to wear fake things, saying that they are not real and there is no interest in wearing them.

Speaking of those who became rich through divorce, there is also Kay Francis. She also has two treasures, an emerald ring and a large diamond. Both are souvenirs from her two ex-husbands. These two things are now also stored in a bank in New York, and she doesn't dare to bring them to Hollywood. In addition to Marion Davies, the Talmadge sisters are also considered wealthy. The other stars, like Joan Crawford and Carole Lombard, also have very valuable things, but they are all stored in banks and cannot be revealed. The rest need not be said.

Film Reviews

Review of "Brothers' Blood"

— Ling He

— Produced by Anwen Company, premiered at the Beijing Theater —

If we acknowledge that Chinese films have indeed improved, then these large companies with relatively strong capital can achieve their proper results, while many small companies still have no way to develop. This phenomenon is not only unique to China. For example, in the United States, Columbia Pictures is generally not as good as MGM or other large companies with strong capital.

But I always think that no matter how small the company is, at least the story of the film should be made better. We always feel disgusted with Columbia's constant martial arts films, and that is the reason.

"Brothers' Blood" can be said to be very naive and ridiculous from the script to the performance, especially the story of revenge.

Let's think about it. Simply depicting vulgar love is already a superficial expression, let alone demanding that men and women who originally didn't know what "sacred love" was be faithful to honest love; or trying to write simple things between men and women as celestial beings, which cannot help but make people laugh. In addition, explaining jealousy and murder with stale talks such as "harming others harms oneself first... the net of heaven is inescapable" is especially old-fashioned and vulgar.

In terms of performance, it is like elementary school students writing compositions. We only ask for fluency, but the director of "Brothers' Blood" didn't even achieve this point, let alone anything else?

However, to lower the standards a bit, the scene of a small bird in a tree is still good-looking. In addition, the minor mistakes are simply countless.

I hope that the authors of "Brothers' Blood" will work harder.

Review of "Risky Encounter"

— Moore

Last Trail

The romance of "hero and beauty" is dramatic and has been adopted by filmmakers for a long time. Because this type of film is imaginary and the formula has gradually been rejected by the audience, it seems that filmmakers have not completely abandoned this type of story, so in the current decline of Western films, we still see this "Risky Encounter."

General criticisms of martial arts films are already sufficient. At the same time, because this type of film is "stereotyped" (more formulaic than formulaic), criticism of this type of film also has to be more repetitive; although this cannot be used to prove the formulaic nature of film criticism, it is at least a "waste" because audiences have long become the most accurate and strictest critics.

Because of the outdated content, new forms naturally will not arise. Our director should first propose economics when dealing with this story. He first concentrates the material of the story, and then removes its branches and leaves. This is because the director also knows that all martial arts films are disliked by the audience. If many old scenes are displayed in full, it will only deepen the audience's disgust, so he only narrates quickly and concisely.

However, the producers of "Risky Encounter," although abandoning many disgusting elements, immediately fell into another evil path. That is the addition of comedy, which he may think is too monotonous in the story that has been stripped of its branches and leaves, so he added some jokes to adjust it. However, this kind of bad and unreasonable work only destroys the atmosphere.

This is the end of the discussion of "Risky Encounter" itself. Below, I would like to explain the comparison between modern American martial arts films and "Don Quixote." "Don Quixote," whether the author of the novel or the author of the film, expresses sympathy for the fate of "Don Quixote" in the same way. However, the producers of modern American films are completely fantasizing about "chivalrous and generous" heroes. In "Don Quixote," we see the decline of ancient knights. Therefore, it is more realistic, while modern American martial arts films are simply daytime dreams with no reality at all. If we use reality to criticize the value of works, then this is easy to understand.

Martial arts films have been handed over to a declining fate. Here, we see the future of film!

Audience Opinions

My Opinion on "Evil Neighbors"

— Fu

Yueming Film Company, which has always specialized in producing "Kanto Heroes" and "Female Bodyguards," has recently changed its style and produced works of the times.

Strictly speaking, the ideology and plot of "Evil Neighbors" feel too ideal and too complex. The worst thing is that they also inserted a section of what (?) "Kunlun Mountain Female Knight" to stage a martial arts fight, and committed the inherent problem. This has to be a pity for Yueming Company. However, the motive of the author of the script for this film is still very admirable.

Of course, a film does not rely entirely on the correctness of consciousness. The efforts of the actors are also part of the relationship. The first few actors in "Evil Neighbors" made efforts, including Zhang Yuting and Wang Feijuan, who were also very good. He Feiguang's insidiousness is not bad.

The director's skills are not bad. The photography is much better than before. In short, this "Evil Neighbors" is much better than Yueming Company's previous films. It is also very rare among the small companies.

"Evil Neighbors" - My Review

— Ding Ding

What surprised me was the photography. Not only was it unlike the output of a small company as generally imagined, but it was also sufficient to compete with the output of large companies. Except for a few shots where the light was a little too strong, the entire film was exceptionally clear and lovely, and the scene transitions were very novel and chic.

The director's techniques are clever and flexible. He can use some small tricks to give the audience some amusement. However, there are two points that I cannot help but question.

(1) Where exactly is Huang Youjia, the silkworm farmer, located - in the countryside, or in the same bustling city as Huang Huaren? Raising silkworms in a bustling city is already somewhat far-fetched, and wearing a Western suit to raise silkworms in the countryside would probably be even more unrealistic! And why do all the hooligans have to wear tattered Western suits?

(2) One evening, when Huang Huaren and Zhihua were enjoying the moon in the garden, they were both wearing light clothing. But soon after, when Zhihua pulled Huaren out to buy a jade bottle, Zhihua was already wearing a leather short jacket. Did the weather change that quickly?

In terms of the actors, the ones playing Huang Huaren and Wu Zhihua are both suitable, especially the one playing the servant Cai Ma-fu, whose movements are natural and without the affected attitude of a typical servant portrayal. The one playing Guofen seems to have too few expressions.

Finally, I should say that "Evil Neighbors" is always worth seeing.

Film Novel

Shanghai 24 Hours (7)

— Tian Fu

The air in the room was so heavy it felt like it was about to explode. The distant sound of a whistle announced that it was noon. Old Chen's wife sadly raised her head, thinking: the deceased's sister is still sweating away at work in the factory, the fate of this family...

Old Zhao, who was silently weeping, suddenly spoke, asking Chen Da's wife: "Why hasn't his older brother returned?"

"Him?" Old Chen's wife widened her eyes, as if a bomb had exploded in her head: "The heavens are blind! Last night, the comprador's house was robbed, and they insist it was him... They arrested him and put him in jail." Then, she continued in a ghostly monologue: "One dead, one in jail... the whole family is finished... finished, everything is finished..."

As she said this, Old Zhao's complexion suddenly underwent a dramatic change: one moment flushed red, the next turning ashen, with sweat streaming down his head. He did not want to inadvertently being a "substitute for the scapegoat" to harm his friend. He was deeply distressed, feeling that a huge violence was ravaging his soul. Old Chen's wife looked at him in amazement. He shouted violently: "I stole that thing, that thing! I can't implicate you, I'll turn myself in! I'll turn myself in!"

When she suddenly realized the inside story of this matter from her surprise and doubt, Old Zhao had already run madly out of the door like a wild beast who lost his humanity.

(10) An Ordinary Day

Two hours later. Old Chen, who was confusedly imprisoned in jail, was anxiously fretting: suddenly a jailer escorted Old Zhao into the jail wearing shackles. He looked at Old Zhao in surprise, but Old Zhao smiled and went to him. He was wondering: how did Old Zhao get arrested too? But another jailer suddenly came in and released him.

Like a little bird escaping from its cage, Old Chen flew home.

Old Chen's wife was surprised when she saw her husband suddenly return, and she also felt a trace of relief; but when she thought of the reason her husband was released, the scene of Old Zhao shouting "I'll turn myself in!" and running out madly flashed through her mind; she was also moved to sudden tears.

Old Chen's eyes were fixed on that small bed, the corpse of their younger brother, who had lost his life, lying stiffly there: two incense sticks were burning on the bed. The incense smoke curled upwards, rising into the space, disappearing from sight. Old Chen's heart, however, kept sinking, sinking, sinking...

Time passed ordinarily for a day: it was four o'clock. The arteries of the metropolis were still throbbing violently. The comprador's wife got out of bed again, drinking chicken broth, thinking about how to squander this night in wild revelry.

Cars, foreign-style houses, women, mesmerizing dances...

Unemployment, injury, imprisonment, death...

Every day, every day, cycling day and night. Shanghai is forever so lively, brilliant, and magnificent... (The End)
